# v10.3 corpus source-admission implementation plan

> **For agentic workers:** REQUIRED SUB-SKILL: Use
> `superpowers:subagent-driven-development` (recommended) or
> `superpowers:executing-plans` to implement this plan task-by-task. Use
> `superpowers:test-driven-development` for every code task and
> `superpowers:verification-before-completion` before each commit. Steps use
> checkbox (`- [ ]`) syntax for tracking.

**Goal:** Turn the centralized v10.3 source inventory into a deterministic,
reviewed eligible-count census and admit only provenance-backed AI-positive and
human-negative code units, before any corpus manifest, selection, run, or
calibration promotion is created.

**Architecture:** Keep the corpus storage root at
`/Users/cheng/corpus-expansion`. The v10.3 directory is the control-plane and
review root: pinned benchmark/controlled bytes live under
`v10.3/sources/`, while the centralized legacy inventory bytes live once under
the parent `positive/` and `negative/` arms; `v10.3/sources/legacy-*` are
internal references, not independent source copies. Admission records and
review decisions live under `v10.3/review/admission/`. A schema-backed, fail-closed
admission verifier derives eligibility from immutable source, rights,
authorship, edit-lineage, family, pair, cluster, privacy, and overlap evidence;
it never infers eligibility from a directory or raw row count. A separate
deterministic census command writes one canonical artifact, and only a reviewed
`smoke.ready: true` census bound to an exact reverified witness may feed the
explicit witness-to-manifest builder in Task 9B. Core owns only persisted JSON
contracts and pure durable validators. SlopBrick owns offline byte resolution,
the unforgeable in-process verified-context brand, disposition derivation,
authority builders, and census I/O. Shared release-archive contracts are
implemented once by the release-asset plan and imported here; admission never
forks a second archive or receipt shape.

**Tech Stack:** TypeScript compiled by the current tsup `node18` target and run
under the package's current Node `>=20` contract, JSON Schema draft 2020-12,
AJV, Vitest, the existing canonical JSON/SHA-256 helpers, reviewed admission-
specific exact-overlap primitives, Git plumbing behind a validated CLI, and
source-specific read-only audit adapters. Admission code may not use a Node
22/24-only API until the separate runtime-policy tranche changes the package,
types, build target, CI matrices, and packed-consumer evidence together.
No candidate code is imported or executed. The external-only Droid Parquet
adapter uses the already-created corpus review environment, Python 3.14.4 and
`pyarrow==25.0.0`; those are recorded in its ledger and are not added to the
TypeScript monorepo.

## Global constraints

- The canonical corpus storage workspace is `/Users/cheng/corpus-expansion`;
  `/Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3` is the canonical v10.3 control-plane,
  review, quarantine, and artifact root. No corpus path may depend on the
  former `/Users/cheng/ai-slop-baseline` location.
- `AI -> verified_ai` is the positive polarity and
  `human -> verified_human` is the negative polarity. Folder names and legacy
  `positive`/`negative` arms are intake declarations only.
- Do not create a manifest, selection, run, checkout map, promotion, model, or
  signal-strength patch while executing Tasks 1-8 of this plan.
- Do not clone, fetch, download, or acquire another public source until the
  first deterministic census is generated and independently reviewed.
- Raw inventory counts, filesystem counts, source-register counts, dataset
  rows, and directory membership are never eligible counts.
- The **initial** composed admission register has exactly 329 entries (12
  original register entries plus 317 repository-inventory material leaves).
  Every current entry has exactly one schema-valid `source-review.json`, even
  when the truthful decision is `source_quarantine`; an omitted review is a
  hard census error. Promoting an existing leaf preserves that count. A later
  explicitly authorized acquisition may append a new material-source entry
  only together with its acquisition receipt, register-delta receipt, closed
  inventory, and matching source review; census validation then requires exact
  equality against that larger current ID set.
- The census reports both eligible record counts and deduplicated eligible
  code-unit counts. Smoke/canary deficits use unique content units, never raw
  records; within one label a content cluster's canonical counting owner is
  the lexicographically smallest eligible `recordId`.
- The census also reports registered candidate units that have not yet been
  normalized into admission records. Source-wide quarantine may explain those
  units, but it may not hide them or turn them into a zero-sized denominator.
- Preserve legacy source bytes, labels, ordering, membership, and count
  semantics as immutable discovery input. The 2026-07-13 centralization is a
  receipt-bound path-only derived generation: its preimage snapshot and exact
  prefix mapping live in
  `v10.3/quarantine/legacy-filelists-pre-centralization-2026-07-13`, and it does
  not relabel, resample, or promote any record.
- Preserve existing dirty and untracked platform files. Stage only the exact
  files named by each commit boundary.
- Use `corepack pnpm`; do not use a global `pnpm`.
- Do not push, tag, publish, deploy, alter a remote, contact a maintainer, or
  upload a corpus bundle without explicit owner authorization.
- An archive, Parquet shard, CSV, or JSONL container is not a scannable code
  unit. Its embedded records remain ineligible until a versioned projection
  produces independently hashable files and an immutable supported
  materialization binds those files.
- Static inspection only: never import, compile, run, test, or execute
  candidate corpus code.
- Every executable admission action names one schema-valid task-scoped tool
  profile. A broad host-level receipt cannot authorize a narrower task, and a
  receipt from one profile cannot be replayed under another.

### Frozen execution baseline for this plan

The inspected host baseline is macOS 26.5.1, zsh 5.9, Node 24.15.0 and
Corepack 0.34.6 at
`/Users/cheng/.local/share/mise/installs/node/24.15.0/bin/`, Corepack pnpm
9.15.0, `/usr/bin/git` 2.50.1 (Apple Git-155), `/usr/bin/jq` 1.7.1-apple,
`/usr/bin/shasum` 6.02, and BSD `/usr/bin/du` (`-k`, not GNU
`--version`). The external review interpreter is
`/Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3/review/.venv/bin/python`, Python 3.14.4,
with `pyarrow==25.0.0`.

Task 0 bootstraps these observations, but its prose output is not eligibility
evidence. The first vertical contract slice defines canonical tool-profile and
tool-receipt schemas; Task 0 is then rerun to emit schema-valid receipts and
verifies behavior, not merely version strings. Shell arithmetic involving
`du -k` is forbidden as an authority; the Node CLI uses `lstat`, safe integers,
and streamed byte counters. Python audits always use the exact interpreter,
`-B`, and `PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE=1`. A different host may proceed only after
the same behavioral probes pass and its local-only tool receipt hash is bound
in the evidence document. Node 22/24 matrix adoption remains a hard dependency
before manifest/smoke execution, but not a pretext for using unshipped APIs in
Tasks 1-8.

### Frozen task-scoped tool profiles

The policy contains these exact profile IDs. Each profile is a durable Core
artifact, and each invocation produces a durable receipt bound to the profile,
canonical arguments, input hashes, executable identity/behavior probes, exit
status, and output hashes. Host paths and environment-specific timestamps stay
in an adjacent local diagnostic, never in the canonical receipt.

| Profile ID | Allowed authority surface | Network policy | Resource policy |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `admission-core-contract-v1` | Node, Corepack pnpm, Core schema/codegen/test commands | denied | no candidate-byte access |
| `admission-context-v1` | Node plus read-only Git `cat-file`/`rev-parse` against registered local object stores | denied; all proxy/credential/askpass variables cleared | at most one evidence/CAS object open at once |
| `admission-static-ledgers-v1` | Node normalizers, external sort, privacy/quality/lineage builders | denied | 64 MiB shards, 64 open files, 4 GiB V8 heap, 6 GiB maximum RSS, 200 GiB work-directory ceiling, 32 MiB per code unit, 24-hour wall ceiling |
| `admission-census-v1` | Node canonical parser, feasibility solver, transactional filesystem writer | denied | smoke 10,000,000 and canary 50,000,000 search nodes |
| `admission-manifest-v1` | Node plus exact `git-readonly-object-v1` (`/usr/bin/git rev-parse`/`cat-file` only) for approved-commit objects; verified ready-context/prerequisite reader; no-clobber prerequisite/manifest publishers and recoveries | denied; Git proxy/credential/config/askpass variables cleared | reads only approved Git objects or closed staging inputs; writes the contained prerequisite CAS/projection/completion lock+transaction or one contained `manifests/` generation |
| `admission-acquisition-publication-v1` | Node metadata-index/register publication and explicit recovery actions only | denied | fixed acquisition/register/evidence metadata paths, one lock/transaction, no candidate execution |
| `admission-source-node-v1` | Node and read-only registered Git plumbing for one named source adapter | denied | source-specific reviewed record cap |
| `admission-source-parquet-v1` | exact Python 3.14.4 + `pyarrow==25.0.0`, read-only Droid shards | denied | exact 400-row preregistered sample; no projected code output |
| `admission-acquisition-round-v1` | Node transaction/orchestration over reviewed source authorizations; invokes only exact child capabilities | denied directly | at most two sources, one 5 GiB cumulative reservation, one active round lock |
| `admission-git-acquire-v1` | isolated `/usr/bin/git` fetch plus `ls-tree`/`cat-file`; no checkout | exact approved credential-free HTTPS Git origin only | 5 GiB materialized hard cap; transport bytes explicitly unbounded by stock Git |
| `admission-release-acquire-v1` | shared release-asset HTTPS downloader and safe ZIP materializer only | exact approved HTTPS URL/redirect set only | 5 GiB streamed-transfer and 5 GiB materialized hard caps |
| `admission-evidence-acquire-v1` | shared hardened HTTPS downloader into the evidence CAS only; no archive interpretation | one exact authorized immutable evidence URL/redirect set only | exact expected media type/hash/bytes, 64 MiB default and authorization-bound hard transfer cap |

`git-readonly-object-v1` resolves only the reviewed absolute `/usr/bin/git`
executable and permits argument-array invocations equivalent to
`rev-parse --verify <40hex>^{commit}` plus `cat-file -e|-s|-p
<40hex>:<normalized-relative-path>`. It forbids shell use, `-c`/config
overrides, replace/graft refs, worktree reads, ref discovery, hooks, and every
network-capable subcommand. The executable behavior probe hash is part of each
intent/receipt; a different host must pass the same probe before its executable
ID is admitted.

`allowedActions` is not free-form in a valid profile. It must equal the sorted,
duplicate-free row below exactly; an extra, missing, aliased, or cross-profile
action is a semantic error.

| Profile | Exact `allowedActions` |
| --- | --- |
| `admission-core-contract-v1` | `core:contract` |
| `admission-context-v1` | `census:preview`, `context:verify`, `evidence:verify`, `lint`, `manifest:verify`, `manifest:verify-prerequisites`, `source:census` |
| `admission-static-ledgers-v1` | `authority:overlap`, `authority:overlap:recover`, `authority:overlap:verify`, `authority:remaining`, `rebuild:pre-witness`, `static-authority:recover` |
| `admission-census-v1` | `census`, `census:current-hash`, `census:recover`, `census:stdout`, `require`, `verify`, `witness:constraint-check`, `witness:publish-review`, `witness:publish-search`, `witness:recover-publication`, `witness:regenerate`, `witness:search` |
| `admission-manifest-v1` | `manifest:build`, `manifest:publish-prerequisites`, `manifest:recover`, `manifest:recover-prerequisites` |
| `admission-acquisition-publication-v1` | `acquisition:authorize`, `acquisition:publish`, `acquisition:recover-publication`, `evidence:recover`, `register:publish-round`, `register:recover` |
| `admission-source-node-v1` | `source:audit-node` |
| `admission-source-parquet-v1` | `source:audit-parquet` |
| `admission-acquisition-round-v1` | `acquire:recover`, `acquire:round` |
| `admission-git-acquire-v1` | `acquire:git-child` |
| `admission-release-acquire-v1` | `acquire:release-child` |
| `admission-evidence-acquire-v1` | `evidence:acquire` |

Commands reject a missing/wrong profile before reading candidate bytes. The
networked profiles require a one-use authorization hash and cannot be selected
by census, context, ledger, review, or manifest commands. Tests replace spawn,
DNS, socket/HTTP dispatch, and environment boundaries and prove every
non-allowlisted path stays unreachable.

### Shared release-asset prerequisite and single Core owner

Before admission Task 1A modifies Core, Tasks 1-6 of
`packages/slopbrick/docs/calibration/v10.3-release-asset-materialization-plan.md`
must be implemented, pass their gates, and receive independent approval. That
tranche is the sole owner of `ReleaseArchiveMaterialization`,
`MaterializationReceiptV1`, archive identity, safe ZIP rules, the offline
materialization resolver, and their Core exports/generated types. Admission
imports those exact exports and JSON Schema `$ref`s; it must not recreate,
rename, widen, or regenerate a competing shape. Release-plan Tasks 7-8 are
**downstream** consumers of this admission plan: Task 4 records EvalPlus as
quarantined evidence, admission Tasks 5-8 decide whether any EvalPlus units
are eligible, Task 9B creates the only admission-backed manifest path, and only
then may release-plan Task 7 consume that approved admission manifest and
create a run when it contains exact EvalPlus witness units; it never creates a
second/direct EvalPlus manifest. Release-plan Task 8 follows that decision.
The release plan must not create `manifests/`, `selection/`, or `runs/` as a
prerequisite to admission.

The release tasks and admission Core slices are sequential single-writer work:
no agent may edit `packages/core/schemas/v1/index.json`, Core exports, codegen,
or shared generated files for both plans concurrently. A clean merge-base,
green release-plan gate receipt, and `git diff --check` are recorded before
Task 1A starts.

### Coordinated Core schema tranche

Shared release-plan Task 1 plus admission Tasks 1A-3B and 9A-9B are one
unreleased, branch-local Core schema tranche. At the start of release-plan Task
1 (the first Core schema change), bump private `@usebrick/core` from `0.2.0` to `0.3.0`,
change SlopBrick's dev dependency from `workspace:*` to
`workspace:^0.3.0`, update `pnpm-lock.yaml`, and record the admission-contract
tranche in `packages/core/README.md`. All later Core schema slices in this plan
must land on that same branch before release; `0.3.0` is not published as a
partial tranche. Task 9B's final SlopBrick `0.45.0` CHANGELOG/release commit is
the consuming-package version boundary and revalidates the exact Core version,
workspace range, generated peers, lockfile, and bundled output. Any Core schema
change outside this enumerated tranche requires a new Core version and matching
SlopBrick workspace-range update.

The admission schemas are additions, and `admissionBinding` is optional for
legacy corpus manifests as defined in Task 9B, so this plan does not change the
four existing Repository Structure schemas' required fields and does not bump
`STRUCTURE_SCHEMA_VERSION`.

---

## 1. Authority, snapshot, and what “eligible” means

This plan closes Gap 1 in
`.superpowers/sdd/v045-execution-reconciliation.md`. Its evidence snapshot is
the external workspace as inspected on 2026-07-11 (Europe/Lisbon), especially:

- `review/source-register.json`;
- `review/repository-inventory.json`;
- `review/{positive,negative}-v5-file-inventory.jsonl`;
- `review/calibration-readiness-review.md`;
- `review/labeling-protocol-v1.md`;
- `review/humaneval-controlled-audit.json` and its provenance review;
- `review/evalplus-v0.1.0-audit.json` and its consistency tests;
- `review/ai-strong-authorship-candidates.json`;
- `review/ai-repository-review-priority.json`;
- the pinned local checkouts and payloads in `sources/benchmarks/`.

At this snapshot:

- the source register has 12 source entries;
- the raw legacy discovery arms contain 635,830 declared-AI and 842,520
  declared-human files (1,478,350 total); this is an open discovery population,
  never an additive reviewed-record denominator;
- the legacy selected review inventory has 452,382 hashed records
  (224,903 declared AI and 227,479 declared human);
- those 452,382 selected records partition exactly into 58,089 baseline
  material units (5,809 declared AI + 52,280 declared human with no
  `repositoryId`) and 394,293 repository-mapped material units; the baseline
  and selected-inventory register rows must not both add the same 58,089;
- the controlled HumanEval cohort has 100 AI and 100 human candidates, eight
  content-unsafe pair groups, a conditional content-safe upper bound of 92 AI
  + 92 human units, and zero eligible records because its exact bundle/evidence
  is not at an immutable supported HTTPS source;
- EvalPlus has 164 + 164 audited files and zero eligible records;
- `manifests/`, `selection/`, and `runs/` contain no files;
- therefore the current reviewed eligible census is exactly
  `verified_ai = 0`, `verified_human = 0`.

That zero is a correct result, not a lack of corpus volume. The first
implementation run must reproduce it from normalized admission inputs before
any remediation is allowed to increase it.

An eligible code unit is one exact byte sequence with all of these properties:

1. It has a canonical admission record and a unique record ID.
2. Its raw source, immutable revision or asset digest, logical locator,
   byte count, and SHA-256 all agree.
3. A rights reviewer has approved the exact intended use and, when derived
   bundles are involved, redistribution of that exact unit.
4. Its polarity is supported by accepted AI or human evidence at the scope of
   that exact unit.
5. AI records have a resolved generator and human-edit status; human records
   have an accepted human-provenance route.
6. Family, pair, exact-cluster, near-cluster, language, and stratum identities
   are present and globally consistent.
7. Syntax/quality, privacy, secret, scaffold, and overlap gates pass.
8. Two independent reviewers agree, and the generic verifier recomputes the
   same disposition from their bound evidence.

No field named `eligible` in a source-specific audit is trusted by itself.
The generic verifier derives the final disposition.

---

## 2. Prior art, primary-source research, and explicit inferences

The upstream facts below were rechecked against official primary sources on
2026-07-11. Commit-specific links are preferred so a later README change does
not rewrite the review basis.
The rights fields below are conservative project-admission controls, not legal
advice or a declaration that an upstream publisher lacks rights.

### 2.1 Verified upstream facts

- [HumanEval at the pinned commit](https://github.com/openai/human-eval/blob/6d43fb980f9fee3c892a914eda09951f772ad10d/README.md)
  calls itself a hand-written evaluation set, and the pinned repository has an
  [MIT license](https://github.com/openai/human-eval/blob/6d43fb980f9fee3c892a914eda09951f772ad10d/LICENSE).
- [LPcode at the pinned commit](https://github.com/Shinwoo-Park/LPcode/blob/b3660c8262ae57e14498528119607ee673d4257a/README.md)
  claims 4,271 human snippets and four 4,271-snippet LLM arms across C, C++,
  Java, and Python. It says the human snippets came from 2019-2020 GitHub
  repositories with Apache/BSD/MIT licenses and names ChatGPT, Gemini-Pro,
  WizardCoder, and DeepSeek-Coder as paraphrasers.
- The pinned LPcode Git tree has no root or nested `LICENSE`, `LICENCE`, or
  `COPYING` file. The local Task 1 payload has 34,168 JSONL rows, 4,272
  distinct raw `file_name` strings, and 4,275 distinct
  `(language, file_name)` pairs: Python 1,936; Java 1,495; C 458; C++ 386. The
  per-language pairs are four above the README total. Rows split evenly between
  Task 1 labels 0 and 1, while every row still has both `human_src` and
  `llm_src`; that Task 1 label is not an authorship polarity.
- The pinned BigCodeBench repository contains an
  [Apache-2.0 LICENSE](https://github.com/bigcode-project/bigcodebench/blob/09dd993f46c3fbf3a799465bb96d524edcb0b199/LICENSE).
  Its [pinned official README](https://github.com/bigcode-project/bigcodebench/blob/09dd993f46c3fbf3a799465bb96d524edcb0b199/README.md)
  points to model-generated samples in the
  [v0.2.4 release](https://github.com/bigcode-project/bigcodebench/releases/tag/v0.2.4).
  Those generated samples are not present in the current 772 KiB local
  checkout.
- The pinned
  [DroidCollection dataset card](https://huggingface.co/datasets/project-droid/DroidCollection/blob/9a42843be99456a3af70d2b9c9a53a4d7624598f/README.md)
  declares human, machine-generated, machine-refined, and adversarial labels,
  generator/source/language fields, and 1,058,248 records, but its YAML metadata
  has no `license` field. Hugging Face's
  [dataset-card documentation](https://huggingface.co/docs/hub/datasets-cards)
  identifies `license` as the metadata field used to declare dataset terms.
- The pinned
  [Monize README](https://github.com/kenlasko/monize/blob/930eff4f31562366fa0d972e0ff4d33b8b497371/README.md)
  says the project is “100% written by AI,” with “practically zero manual
  changes,” and names Claude Code. The pinned tree contains AGPL-3.0 at license
  SHA-256 `0d96a4ff68ad6d4b6f1f30f713b18d5184912ba8dd389f86aa7710db079abcb0`.
  The legacy review inventory has 1,772 unique selected hashes for this repo.
- The pinned
  [Magic8Ball README](https://github.com/statico/magic8ball/blob/a1afcbc83704454a5b854f9518847c82c1d7b7dc/README.md)
  says most Swift code was written by ChatGPT 3.5, but also documents extensive
  human fixing and iteration; its Git tree has no license.
- The pinned
  [ProgramsGeneratedByChatGPT README](https://github.com/RaphaelKhoury/ProgramsGeneratedByChatGPT/blob/79e915a7de7653571a87ff3e7a66118e0bfaa66b/Readme.md)
  describes an initial and an interactively corrected ChatGPT 3.5 program set;
  its Git tree has no license.
- GitHub's official
  [repository licensing guidance](https://docs.github.com/en/enterprise-cloud@latest/repositories/managing-your-repositorys-settings-and-features/customizing-your-repository/licensing-a-repository)
  states that without a license, default copyright law applies and others may
  not generally reproduce, distribute, or create derivative works. The same
  guidance notes that users may view and fork a public repository under
  GitHub's Terms of Service; view/fork permission is not a dataset
  redistribution or derivative-bundle license.

### 2.2 Inferences that must not be promoted to facts

- LPcode's statement that upstream human repositories used permissive
  licenses does **not** establish a license for the LPcode dataset, a complete
  per-record upstream rights chain, or permission to republish its LLM outputs.
  This is a rights-review blocker, not an accusation about the dataset.
- BigCodeBench's repository license does **not by itself** prove that every
  release-asset sample and every embedded benchmark scaffold is covered by the
  same terms. Asset scope must be recorded explicitly before acquisition.
- The absence of `license:` in DroidCollection's dataset-card metadata means
  no license is declared through that official channel. It does not prove that
  no rights exist elsewhere; it requires a primary-source license decision.
- Monize is stronger repository-scope AI evidence than a keyword hit, but
  “practically zero” does not identify which files were manually changed and
  does not supply per-file prompt/model revision records. Without a scoped
  attestation, its exact files are `humanEditStatus = unknown`, not strict
  smoke gold.
- HumanEval's hand-written claim supports human provenance, but a locally
  reconstructed `.py` module is still a derived unit. It becomes eligible only
  when its derivation and immutable materialization are truthfully represented.
- A pre-2020 Git blob is strong historical evidence against modern LLM coding,
  but timestamp/history is an inferential human-provenance route, not direct
  proof of a person's keystrokes. Records using it must say
  `humanEvidenceKind = historical_inference`.

### 2.3 Prior-art decision

- **Adopt:** retain the controlled HumanEval and EvalPlus static audit methods,
  frozen 5-token/0.80 near-duplicate threshold, source register, closed
  inventories, and two-reviewer protocol as evidence inputs.
- **Extend:** add admission-specific Core schemas and semantic verification;
  do not overload the existing corpus manifest with incomplete candidates.
- **Compose:** reuse canonical JSON/SHA-256, exact content hashing, release-
  asset materialization, and the existing v10.3 selection verifier after
  admission. Existing MinHash/LSH remains diagnostic-only; it is not reused as
  the gold no-near-overlap authority.
- **Build:** add the missing generic admission ledger and deterministic census,
  because no current tool produces an exact, fail-closed eligible count across
  heterogeneous source audits.

---

## 3. Frozen source ranking and bounded review batches

Raw size is not the ranking signal. Rank by the shortest path to exact,
reviewable, diverse eligible units.

| Rank | Already-present candidate | Current usable count | Why it is ranked here | Mandatory stop before promotion |
| ---: | --- | ---: | --- | --- |
| 1 | Controlled HumanEval GPT-5 cohort | 0 eligible; at most 92 verified-AI + 92 verified-human content-safe units projected only after the global source blockers are resolved | Exact prompts, outputs, hashes, no-human-edit claims, canonical human pairing, and a fail-closed audit already exist | Immutable supported publication/materialization plus immutable generator evidence; re-audit and two-reviewer approval |
| 2 | LPcode | 0 | Four languages, named generators, explicit human/LLM fields, and paired tasks make it the highest-yield embedded-record candidate | Dataset/output license scope; per-record upstream human origin/license; README 4,271 vs local 4,275 language/name-pair reconciliation; record-projection contract; global overlap |
| 3 | Monize | 0 | Strong pinned repository-wide AI authorship statement, 1,772 unique selected hashes, and a root AGPL license | Exact-file scope, third-party/vendor exclusions, model/edit-status resolution, privacy, family/cluster review; strict smoke still requires `humanEditStatus = none` |
| 4 | ProgramsGeneratedByChatGPT | 0 | Small, explicitly named generated/corrected sets and cheap to audit | No license; distinguish initial from corrected/human-interacted files; only 22 initial files are present |
| 5 | BigCodeBench | 0 local generated samples | Official model-sample release and repository license make it a plausible later release-asset source | Generated sample asset is not local; asset license scope, model revisions, scaffold share, human-edit status, and overlap must be preflighted before any download |
| 6 | DroidCollection | 0 | 1,058,248 local rows, nine languages, and rich generator/mode/source fields | No declared dataset license; third-party source rights and item-level origin families unresolved; Parquet records need a versioned projection; mixed/adversarial modes stay separate |
| 7 | Magic8Ball (`magic8ball`, registered) | 0 | Small registered manual-authorship case study | “Most” code claim, extensive human fixing, no license, and third-party assets; not binary gold without exact-file adjudication |
| 8 | PPT Master (`positive-vibe-coded--ppt-master`, legacy leaf only) | 0 | Legacy candidate whose README claim is scoped to example decks | Must CAS-replace that leaf's generation-0 quarantine review with an independently approved review for the same material-source entry/checkout; example-deck scope cannot label the whole repository |
| 9 | AIGCodeSet / Whodunit / EvalPlus StarCoder | 0 | Retained as diagnostic research material | Existing independent reviews already found rights, lineage, scaffold, timestamp, or duplicate blockers; do not reopen without new primary evidence |

**Current decision:** no already-present source can produce an approved 100/100
smoke without new evidence or materialization work. The controlled HumanEval
cohort is closest, but resolving its two global publication/source-contract
blockers would expose at most 92/92 currently content-safe units, and the strict
smoke's source/family cap permits at most 50 units per polarity from it. It
therefore cannot fill canonical 100/100 readiness by itself.

Every bounded sample uses seed
`slopbrick-v10.3-admission-review-v1`. Its selection key is lowercase
`sha256(seed + "\0" + sourceId + "\0" + logicalUnitId)`, and each requested
stratum takes the lexicographically smallest keys. Reviewers receive the
selected IDs sorted by a separately hashed presentation key so source order
does not bias the first reviewer. The sample ledger records the population
hash, strata, requested count, selected IDs/keys, presentation order, and
selection hash in the Core-schema-backed
`CalibrationAdmissionReviewSampleV1` contract in Section 5.0.

### Batch A — highest-value remediation, maximum 2 source reviews

1. Controlled HumanEval: all 200 current code units, but no new generation and
   no publication without explicit owner authorization.
2. LPcode source-level preflight first. Do not inspect more than 128 manually
   sampled pairs (32 per language, eight per named generator)
   until license and row/base-count blockers pass. Automated inventory may
   cover every row because it does not make an eligibility claim.

Stop Batch A as soon as one source-wide rights or identity gate fails. Do not
spend review time on per-record promotion behind a global blocker.

### Batch B — strongest Git-native attestation and small explicit dataset

1. Monize: review at most 64 source files, stratified across backend,
   frontend, database/migrations, scripts/config, and tests. Exclude vendored,
   generated, lock, fixture, migration-output, and third-party files before
   sampling.
2. ProgramsGeneratedByChatGPT: audit all 22 initial and 16 corrected files
   because the set is bounded; keep the arms separate.

Batch B may establish candidate quality, but it cannot override missing
file-scope edit evidence or missing rights.

### Batch C — metadata preflight only, maximum 2 sources

1. BigCodeBench: review pinned repository/release metadata and exact asset
   declarations only. Do not acquire the sample asset in this batch.
2. DroidCollection: review pinned card, schema, existing five Parquet shard
   hashes, and a deterministic 400-row sample (25 records per combination of
   four labels and the four highest-volume languages, seed-bound). Do not
   call sampled rows eligible.

### Batch D — human-negative review after the first census

Prioritize the official HumanEval hand-written route. If it cannot supply the
required count, review historical Git blobs from at least five independent
existing legacy-human repositories. A blob may use the historical-inference
route only when its exact bytes are pinned at or before 2020-01-01, the file
has no later byte changes in the selected materialization, license scope is
approved, history is not a bulk import with unknown origin, and two reviewers
agree. Gold additionally requires a separate schema-valid temporal attestation
produced from the complete non-shallow, non-grafted, non-replaced upstream
commit graph and accepted by two independent blinded provenance reviewers who
were neither the intake operator nor either label reviewer. Without that attestation the
record is at most `eligible_sensitivity`, even when every other gate passes.
Current `negative/` directory membership never satisfies this route.

---

## 4. Canonical workspace layout and single-byte policy

The implementation must converge on this external layout:

```text

│   │   ├── current.json
│   │   ├── publication.lock        # absent when idle
│   │   └── publication-transaction.json # absent when idle
│   └── v10.3-admission-canary/     # same exact layout when canary is approved
├── selection/                      # manifest-derived only
└── runs/                           # selection-derived only
```

The original 12-entry `review/source-register.json` remains immutable input.
Admission composes it with the 317-entry repository inventory into schema-
validated `review/admission/source-register-v1.json`. Every composed entry is
classified as exactly one of:

- `aggregate_inventory`: a coverage/index view that owns no raw candidate
  bytes and never contributes additive candidate or disposition counts; or
- `material_source`: the one source that owns/resolves a candidate unit's
  bytes and is additive exactly once.

Every candidate carries one `materialSourceId` and zero or more sorted
`aggregateSourceIds`. For the frozen current partition,
`legacy-v5-inventory` is an aggregate over exactly 452,382 selected units;
`legacy-ai-slop-baseline` is the material source for exactly 58,089 of them;
and the 317 pinned legacy repository entries are the material sources for the
remaining 394,293. Promoting one repository-inventory entry into the top-level
register changes review granularity, not the aggregate population. The raw
1,478,350-arm discovery count is recorded separately with `closedWorld=false`
and never sums into selected coverage.

The frozen initial composition is generation 0 and contains exactly 329 source
IDs and exactly 329 source-review artifacts. At every later generation, the
source-review ID set must equal the **current** register ID set byte-for-byte;
329 is an initial-snapshot invariant, not a permanent count ceiling. Each
generation above 0 forms one continuous, hash-linked chain from the frozen
generation-0 register through schema-valid acquisition-bound register deltas.
The 317 repository leaves receive real, schema-valid
reviews, not omitted rows or templated nulls: each binds its exact register
entry, pinned checkout/inventory evidence when present, current reviewed
rights/authorship state, `candidateCodeUnitCount`, and the complete truthful
quarantine reasons. An unreviewed leaf uses `decision = source_quarantine`, an
empty reviewer-decision set, and `review_incomplete`; it owns its inventory
coverage but contributes zero eligible records. Promotion replaces that
review through CAS and never creates a 330th register/source-review entry.
Only a genuinely new, owner-authorized acquisition may append entry 330 or
beyond. Its atomic, schema-valid register delta binds the parent and next
register hashes, authorization, acquisition receipt, materialization receipt,
exact new entry, and matching source review, and proves the source and byte
tree were not already registered. Missing, reordered, forked, replayed, or
unauthorized deltas invalidate the current register and every dependent
context/census.

Conservation gates fail unless:

```text
452,382 selected aggregate coverage
  = 58,089 baseline material units
  + 394,293 repository-mapped material units
```

No candidate ID may resolve to two material sources; child material-source
sums must equal their aggregate coverage; and adding/removing an aggregate row
must not change global additive totals.

Byte ownership rules:

1. Git-native files remain in their one pinned checkout. Never copy them into
   `positive/`, `negative/`, `review/`, or `quarantine/`.
2. Raw archives, JSONL, CSV, and Parquet remain once in their registered source
   directory. Review artifacts contain locators and hashes, not copied code.
3. A logical code string embedded in a container is a candidate only. If a
   source passes all non-materialization gates, a deterministic projection may
   write the exact scan units once under
   `sources/derived/$BUNDLE_ID/payload/$LANGUAGE/$CONTENT_SHA256.$EXT`.
4. The derived directory is polarity-neutral. AI/human status exists only in
   admission metadata; the same content hash is never copied into two arm
   directories.
5. A derived bundle is still ineligible until it is published or otherwise
   represented by an approved immutable materialization. Local paths are not
   provenance.
6. Identical code-unit bytes use one content-addressed payload path. Distinct
   provenance records may refer to it, but a global exact cluster prevents
   contradictory polarity or split use.
7. `quarantine/` stores record IDs and reasons, not a second copy of the source
   bytes.

This plan deliberately does not extend `release_archive` into a generic record
extractor. Embedded-record projection is allowed only after a source passes
rights and authorship preflight; its output must then use the already-reviewed
release-asset materialization contract or a separately reviewed successor.

---

## 5. Exact admission contracts

### 5.0 Durable policy, tool, review, and search receipts

The following are persisted authority, not inline-only TypeScript examples.
Each has its own Core JSON Schema, generated type, pure shape/semantic
validator, canonical self-hash rule, fixtures, and mutation tests. Unknown
properties fail. IDs are lowercase SHA-256-derived IDs over canonical JSON
with only that object's own ID/hash field omitted.

State-machine transactions are the explicit exception to “hash the whole
object for the ID”: their stable `transactionId` is derived once from a
schema-enumerated immutable intent projection (operation, authorization/input
hashes, frozen paths, invocation intent, and recovery nonce), with the lock ID/
hash, mutable state/phase/observations, and self-hashes excluded. Before a
fixed-path lock is written, this ID is therefore already known and is stored as
the lock's required `intendedTransactionId`; the transaction later binds the
finished `lockSha256` without changing its ID. `transactionSha256` hashes
the complete **current** transaction including the stable ID and current state,
with only `transactionSha256` omitted. Every transition preserves the ID,
changes the state hash, and is written/fsynced before its mutation boundary.
No implementation may infer the intent projection dynamically; fixtures cover
stable-ID/changing-state-hash behavior at every phase for CAS, acquisition,
register, census, and shard transactions.

Every fixed-lock recovery CLI supports two exclusive selectors: an explicit
`--transaction-id`, or `--from-lock` plus the publisher's fixed root selector
(and gate/manifest ID where applicable). The latter schema-validates the lock,
recomputes and matches `intendedTransactionId`, and safely creates/resumes or
rolls back the exact transaction without directory discovery. Both modes
require the matching recovery nonce and explicit no-live-writer
acknowledgement. Fault suites always include the lock-file fsync and lock-
directory fsync windows before transaction intent exists; an operator never
needs to guess an unwritten transaction ID.

```ts
interface CalibrationAdmissionPolicyV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-policy-v1';
  readonly policyId: 'v10.3-admission-v1';
  readonly initialRegisterEntryCount: 329;
  readonly selectedCoverage: 452382;
  readonly baselineMaterialUnits: 58089;
  readonly repositoryMaterialUnits: 394293;
  readonly labels: {
    readonly positive: 'verified_ai';
    readonly negative: 'verified_human';
  };
  readonly evidenceCasPolicy: 'sha256-wx-fsync-v1';
  readonly overlapPolicy: 'prefix-filter-exact-jaccard-0.80-v1';
  readonly reasonVocabularySha256: string;
  readonly toolProfileSha256s: readonly string[];
  readonly smoke: {
    readonly unitsPerPolarity: 100;
    readonly maxSourceOrFamilyUnitsPerPolarity: 50;
    readonly minimumSourcesPerPolarity: 2;
    readonly minimumFamiliesPerPolarity: 3;
    readonly minimumLanguages: 2;
    readonly minimumUnitsPerRepresentedLanguagePerPolarity: 20;
  };
  readonly canary: {
    readonly unitsPerPolarity: 5000;
    readonly maxSourceUnitsPerPolarity: 500;
    readonly maxFamilyUnitsPerPolarity: 1000;
    readonly minimumSourcesPerPolarity: 10;
    readonly minimumFamiliesPerPolarity: 5;
    readonly minimumLanguages: 3;
    readonly minimumUnitsPerLanguagePerPolarity: 250;
    readonly minimumFamiliesPerLanguagePerPolarity: 3;
    readonly minimumAiGeneratorFamilies: 3;
  };
  readonly policySha256: string;
}

interface AdmissionWitnessPolicyV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-witness-policy-v1';
  readonly policyId: 'v10.3-admission-v1';
  readonly gate: 'smoke' | 'canary';
  readonly algorithm: 'lexicographic-bnb-feasibility-v1';
  readonly seed: 'slopbrick-v10.3-admission-review-v1';
  readonly maxSearchNodes: 10000000 | 50000000;
  readonly constraints: readonly {
    readonly constraintId: string;
    readonly kind: 'exact' | 'minimum' | 'maximum' | 'same_split';
    readonly integerValue?: number;
  }[];
  readonly constraintsSha256: string;
  readonly witnessPolicySha256: string;
}

    readonly stagedRelativePath: string;
    readonly finalRelativePath: string;
    readonly bytes: number;
    readonly sha256: string;
  }[];

    readonly phase:
      | 'intent_fsynced'
      | 'artifacts_staged_fsynced'
      | 'artifacts_promoted'
      | 'index_generation_fsynced'
      | 'next_index_temporary_fsynced'
      | 'index_promoted'
      | 'output_directories_fsynced'
      | 'complete';
  };
  readonly transactionSha256: string;
}

type CalibrationNestedPublicationHandoffV1 = {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-nested-publication-handoff-v1';

          | { readonly kind: 'none_infrastructure' }

              readonly kind: 'profiled';
              readonly receiptId: string;

            };

} & (
  | {
      readonly childKind: 'tool_authority_infrastructure';

      readonly childKind: 'profiled_publication';

      readonly childInvocationIntentRelativePath: string;
      readonly childInvocationIntentSha256: string;
      readonly childInvocationIntentAuthorityHandoffSha256: string;
      readonly childInvocationIntentAuthorityIndexSha256: string;
    }
);

interface CalibrationAdmissionBlindAssignmentV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-blind-assignment-v1';
  readonly assignmentId: string;
  readonly target:
    | { readonly kind: 'source'; readonly sourceId: string }
    | { readonly kind: 'record'; readonly recordId: string }
    | {
        readonly kind: 'temporal_attestation';
        readonly temporalAttestationId: string;
        readonly exactBlobOrContentSha256: string;
      }
    | {
        readonly kind: 'provider_revision_exception';
        readonly recordId: string;
        readonly providerVersioningEvidenceId: string;
      }
    | {
        readonly kind: 'witness';
        readonly witnessSha256: string;
        readonly eligibilitySnapshotSha256: string;
        readonly verifiedContextSha256: string;
      };
  readonly evidenceSetSha256: string;
  readonly protocolEvidenceId: string;
  readonly reviewerIds: readonly [string, string];
  readonly peerMaterialHiddenUntilBothSealed: true;
}

    {

    },

}

interface AdmissionSearchReceiptV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-search-receipt-v1';

}

interface CalibrationAdmissionWitnessReviewReceiptV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-witness-review-receipt-v1';
  readonly receiptId: string;
  readonly witnessSha256: string;
  readonly eligibilitySnapshotSha256: string;
  readonly verifiedContextSha256: string;
  readonly blindReviewReceiptId: string;

  readonly regenerationToolReceiptSha256s: readonly [string, string];

  readonly constraintCheckToolReceiptSha256: string;

interface CalibrationHistoricalTemporalAttestationV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-historical-temporal-attestation-v1';
  readonly attestationId: string;
  readonly repositoryId: string;
  readonly immutableCommitSha: string;
  readonly normalizedPath: string;
  readonly blobSha: string;
  readonly completeCommitGraphSha256: string;
  readonly shallowRepository: false;
  readonly graftsOrReplaceRefsPresent: false;
  readonly introducedCommitSha: string;
  readonly lastChangedCommitSha: string;
  readonly introducedAt: string;
  readonly lastChangedAt: string;
  readonly cutoff: '2020-01-01T00:00:00.000Z';
  readonly bulkImportOrigin: 'ruled_out' | 'indeterminate';
  readonly independentExternalObservation: {
    readonly kind:
      | 'timestamped_source_archive'
      | 'package_registry_artifact'
      | 'release_transparency_log'
      | 'independent_content_archive';
    readonly observedAt: string;
    readonly exactBlobOrContentSha256: string;
    readonly evidenceIds: readonly [string, ...string[]];
    readonly evidenceReceiptIds: readonly [string, ...string[]];
  };
  readonly toolReceiptSha256: string;
}
```

The blind-review ID graph is deliberately acyclic. A pre-decision assignment
binds target, evidence, protocol, and reviewers. Each decision binds only that
`assignmentId`; it never names its peer or a later receipt. After both decision
IDs exist, the protocol auditor emits the post-decision blind-review receipt,
which may name both decisions. Neither decision is rehashed. Witnesses likewise
do not contain review IDs: a later witness-review receipt binds the frozen
witness, two independent regenerations, blind receipt, and reviewer decisions.
The census binds the approved receipt. This order removes the previous
decision-ID/peer-ID and witness/review cycles.

A temporal attestation contains no reviewer decision ID. Its target-specific
blind assignment exists first; two independent provenance reviewers then seal
matching `temporal_attestation: accepted` decisions; the post-decision blind
receipt binds those IDs. Historical gold requires that complete acyclic chain.
One embedded or unblinded provenance decision is never sufficient.

`AdmissionWitnessPolicyV1.constraints` is not a second editable policy. Its
canonical constraint IDs and integer values must be a lossless expansion of
the matching `CalibrationAdmissionPolicyV1.smoke` or `.canary` fields,
including every language, source, family, pair/split, and AI-generator-family
floor/cap. Semantic validation recomputes `constraintsSha256` from the durable
admission policy and rejects an omitted, added, or changed constraint.

A Git commit graph and authored/committed timestamps are self-asserted source
metadata and cannot independently establish pre-cutoff existence. The temporal
attestation is gold-capable only when `independentExternalObservation` binds
the exact blob/content through schema-valid, byte-reverified evidence receipts
from an independent timestamped archive, package registry artifact, release
transparency log, or equivalent content archive, and `observedAt <=
2020-01-01T00:00:00.000Z`. Git history without that observation remains
`eligible_sensitivity` at most. Both provenance reviewers must be independent
of intake and both authorship reviewers, and distinct from each other.

### 5.1 Source review

Every source directory binds one `source-review.json`. Rights and origin claims
refer to proof-carrying evidence IDs defined in Section 5.2; a URL/hash string
inside the review is not evidence by itself.


`AdmissionArtifactReceiptV1.pathBase` prevents every hash-named-generation
fixed point across source, input, overlap, static, witness-independent, and
manifest-supporting authorities. `generation_local` paths are normalized fixed
leaf/subtree names resolved only relative to the already-verified immutable
generation directory; they may not contain `generations/`, the generation SHA,
an absolute/root prefix, or `..`. A generation is assembled in a transaction-
bound staging directory, all leaf receipts and the generation object are
hashed, the generation SHA is computed, and only then is the whole directory
no-clobber promoted to `generations/$GENERATION_SHA256` and its parent fsynced.
`admission_root_content_addressed` is allowed only for independently
content-addressed CAS/evidence objects whose root-relative path is uniquely
derived from that object's own hash. Mutable current/flat projection paths are
never generation artifacts. Resolvers join local leaves to the pinned
generation directory and reopen/rehash them; replacement tests re-open every
prior generation after current moves and reject a leaf that resolves through a
flat projection or embeds its outer generation hash.

`record_container` can produce candidate records, but the generic eligibility
predicate always emits `record_container_projection_unsupported` until the
record is rebound to an approved scan-unit materialization.
Its `containers` array is non-empty, sorted by `normalizedPath`, and unique by
path and digest; every path is relative to the registered source root.
`release_archive_set` stores the complete reviewed
`ReleaseArchiveMaterialization` for each asset, including `archiveFormat` and
`rootPrefix`; admission never reconstructs or defaults either field. Each
asset has its own rights decision and maps to one manifest repository ID. The
array is non-empty, unique by `materializationId`, and sorted by that ID.
`materializationId` is `sbm_` plus the canonical SHA-256 of `sourceId`,
`repositoryId`, and the complete materialization object. Heterogeneous asset
rights never inherit silently from `sourceRights`.
An `aggregate_inventory` must use `aggregate_only`, set additive counts false,
and own no admission record. A `material_source` must set additive counts true
and use one supported materialization; semantic validation rejects every other
combination.
`local_unpublished` and `unpublished_bundle` exist only so current blocked
evidence can be represented honestly; they are never eligible materialization
routes.
`localSourceId` is a stable slug, never a filesystem path.
`physicalMemberCount` counts pinned Git files, archive members, or container
rows. `candidateCodeUnitCount` counts code-unit locators after fields are
expanded; for example, one LPcode row containing `human_src` and `llm_src`
contributes one physical member and two candidate code units. The source
census invariant uses candidate units, not physical members.
`sourceRegisterEntrySha256` hashes exactly the source's canonical register
entry, not the changing register as a whole. The census separately binds the
whole canonical register.
Generation 0 has no parent, no deltas, the frozen initial source-ID-set hash,
and exactly 329 entries. Generation `n > 0` has exactly `n` ordered applied
deltas. A delta is derived first and binds only the preceding register plus the
round's one or two new entry/review/acquisition evidence sets; it never embeds the not-yet-derived next
register hash. The following register embeds that delta ID and parent hash.
A later generation receipt binds the completed transaction, delta, and exact
parent/next register hashes plus the one/two immutable source-generation
hashes. They must equal the transaction and final static/current source
pointers after journal cleanup. A post-initial entry's
`acquisitionProvenance` binds only already-existing round, authorization,
source-receipt, and materialization-receipt IDs; it never names the future
delta. The next register records that delta only in `appliedDeltaIds`. The
delta independently binds the entry hash, source generation, successful
receipt, verified materialization, and matching source review. No delta may
modify or delete an earlier entry. Register and matching review publication is
one schema-backed no-clobber/CAS transaction under
`register-generation.lock`. The next immutable source generations and
hash-named register generation are staged/fsynced first. Each source is a
transaction-owned whole staged directory; after its generation hash is known,
the directory is no-clobber promoted to that source's
`generations/$GENERATION_SHA256` path and the exact `generations/` parent is
fsynced. Only then are source-current pointers and the canonical current register
promoted when its expected current hash still matches, and the output
directory is fsynced. While the lock still blocks readers, the tool receipt is
then derived from the completed primary-output projection and indexed through
the single global tool-authority publication transaction. The generation
receipt binds it and is staged/promoted/fsynced under the register lock. Those
later hashes are absent from the frozen
transaction intent and appear only in the discriminated post-output states.
The transaction/lock are removed and their directories fsynced only after the
final register and every receipt revalidate. Context
construction refuses while the lock/transaction exists. Recovery validates
every path/hash/phase, either completes the exact next generation or restores
the prior canonical register and removes only transaction-owned staged bytes,
and is idempotent after every mutation/fsync crash. Two writers cannot publish
the same or forked generation. This one-way
`parent -> delta -> next register -> generation receipt` order has no hash
fixed point. A half-published generation is never authority.
`sourceReviewSha256` is the lowercase SHA-256 of this canonical source-review
object. Admission records bind that review hash as evidence, but it is not part
of their stable code-unit identity.
`reviewerDecisionIds` are sorted, unique references to structured decisions in
Section 5.5. A `candidate` review or any review asserting a resolved authorship,
rights, or eligibility-bearing claim requires at least two distinct reviewers,
authorship and rights role coverage, the exact reviewed evidence set,
blindness attestations, and any adjudication link. A generation-0 leaf whose
only truthful state is `source_quarantine` + `review_incomplete` may use an
empty decision set; it authorizes no claim and contributes zero eligible
records. Every other empty or one-reviewer set is invalid.
The source-generation proposal contains no approval IDs. It is frozen first;
then a separate approval object binds the exact proposal hash, its preassigned
blind assignment, two independent source decisions, and their post-decision
blind receipt. An approval-free generation is valid only through the explicit
`genesis_quarantine` branch for the exact generation-0
`source_quarantine + review_incomplete + []` no-claim snapshot. Every later or
claim-bearing generation must use `independent_review` and resolve the separate
approval object. Validators reject a proposal or register entry that names its
future approval/delta and graph tests prove proposal -> approval -> source
generation -> delta -> next register.

### 5.2 Proof-carrying evidence and materialization receipts

```ts

  readonly evidenceId: string;
  readonly invocationIntentId: string;
  readonly finalRelativePath: string;
  readonly observedBytes: number;
  readonly observedSha256: string;
  readonly networkObservation: {
    readonly requestUrl: string;
    readonly redirectChain: readonly string[];
    readonly resolvedPublicAddresses: readonly string[];
    readonly connectedPeerAddress: string;
    readonly observedMediaType: string;
  };
  readonly networkObservationSha256: string;
  readonly primaryCompletionSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationAdmissionEvidenceCasTransactionV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-evidence-cas-transaction-v1';
  readonly transactionId: string;
  readonly authorizationId: string;
  readonly reservationSha256: string;
  readonly evidenceId: string;
  readonly finalRelativePath: string;
  readonly temporaryRelativePath: string;
  readonly expectedBytes: number;
  readonly expectedSha256: string;
  readonly invocationIntentId: string;
  readonly recoveryNonce: string;
  readonly state:
    | { readonly phase: 'intent_fsynced' }
    | {
        readonly phase:
          | 'network_observation_fsynced'
          | 'temporary_fsynced'
          | 'object_promoted'
          | 'cas_directories_fsynced'
          | 'temporary_removed';
        readonly networkObservationRelativePath: string;
        readonly networkObservationSha256: string;
      }
    | {
        readonly phase: 'cas_complete_waiting_metadata';
        readonly networkObservationRelativePath: string;
        readonly networkObservationSha256: string;
        readonly primaryCompletionRelativePath: string;
        readonly primaryCompletionSha256: string;
      };
  readonly transactionSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationAdmissionEvidenceReceiptV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-evidence-receipt-v1';
  readonly receiptId: string;
  readonly evidenceId: string;
  readonly evidenceIndexSha256: string;
  readonly payloadId: string;
  readonly payloadSetSha256: string;
  readonly verificationMethod:
    | 'offline-materialization-file-v1'
    | 'offline-evidence-cas-v1'
    | 'offline-local-unpublished-reference-v1';
  readonly observedBytes: number;
  readonly observedSha256: string;
  readonly toolReceiptSha256: string;
  readonly status: 'verified' | 'mismatch' | 'unavailable';
}

// Reused exactly from the release-asset plan; no admission-only variant.
interface MaterializationReceiptV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3';
  readonly extractionPolicy: 'safe-zip-v1';
  readonly assetSha256: string;
  readonly assetBytes: number;
  readonly inventorySha256: string;
  readonly entries: readonly {
    readonly path: string;
    readonly kind: 'file' | 'directory';
    readonly bytes?: number;
    readonly sha256?: string;
  }[];
}

interface CalibrationAdmissionMaterializationReceiptV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-materialization-receipt-v1';
  readonly receiptId: string;
  readonly materializationId: string;
  readonly sourceId: string;
  readonly repositoryId: string;
  readonly acquisitionAuthorizationId: string;
  readonly acquisitionAuthorizationSha256: string;
  readonly acquisitionTransactionId: string;
  readonly primaryMaterializedOutputSha256: string;
  readonly childToolReceiptSha256: string;
  readonly verifiedUnitSetSha256: string;
  readonly payload:
    | {
        readonly kind: 'git';
        readonly originUrl: string;
        readonly commitSha: string;
        readonly treeSha: string;
        readonly inventorySha256: string;
      }
    | {
        readonly kind: 'release_archive';
        readonly materialization: ReleaseArchiveMaterialization;
        readonly extractionReceipt: MaterializationReceiptV1;
      };
}
```

IDs are canonical hashes of their objects with the ID/self-hash field omitted.
Items and receipts are sorted and unique by ID. An evidence receipt is valid
only when index byte count/hash, observed byte count/hash, locator semantics,
payload descriptor, actual offline bytes, and task-scoped tool receipt all
agree. Bytes already owned by a verified Git/release materialization must use
`materialization_reference` and are read in place; copying them into evidence
CAS is forbidden. `evidence_cas` is only for immutable HTTPS evidence not
already owned by a source materialization. Its CAS paths are exactly
`review/admission/evidence-cas/sha256/$FIRST_TWO_HEX/$SHA256`, are normalized
relative paths, and are derived rather than caller supplied. Before DNS, a
writer proves the authorization is not already indexed as consumed,
persists/fsyncs its indexed-intent-bound CAS transaction in `intent_fsynced`,
then creates the precomputed authorization reservation with `wx`; a same-
authorization loser removes only its own unstarted transaction and exits before
DNS. A crash before/after reservation creation is recoverable by transaction
ID. Before the first payload byte, the winner advances the reservation-bound
transaction, then opens its transaction-bound sibling temporary with `wx`.
It streams/hash-checks bytes, fsyncs the complete temporary, and atomically
publishes the already-complete inode with a no-clobber same-filesystem hard
link to the final CAS path; it then fsyncs both directories, rehashes the final
object, and unlinks/fsyncs the temporary. Before the CAS transaction can reach
`cas_complete_waiting_metadata`, the exact DNS/redirect/peer/media observations
are written/fsynced to its recorded journal path. That final transaction hash
is not receipt authority; the no-clobber immutable primary-completion object is
written/fsynced next, and its `primaryCompletionSha256` is the only transaction
completion binding used by the acquisition receipt/envelope. The CAS
transaction remains in `evidence-cas/transactions/` until the acquisition
publication transaction has fsynced the receipt, payload/envelope, immutable
index generation, and current index.
An existing same-hash/same-byte final object is idempotent; an occupied path
with different bytes is a hard collision. Direct streaming into the final path
is forbidden. `evidence:recover` requires transaction ID, recovery nonce, and
explicit no-live-writer acknowledgement; it validates the recorded phase,
network observation, CAS bytes, authorization one-use state, and acquisition
index before it links, publishes metadata, unlinks, or resumes. Only after the
indexed envelope revalidates may it unlink/fsync the CAS transaction, then
unlink/fsync the transient one-use reservation, then clean the publication transaction/
lock in their defined order. Unknown files
are never removed. Tests crash after every network-observation, receipt,
payload, envelope, index, transaction-unlink, and directory-fsync boundary and
prove repeated recovery is idempotent. Admission verification is offline and reads only verified in-place
materializations, CAS bytes, or truthful local-unpublished references, never
the original URL or a mutable working tree. `local_unpublished` can
preserve present facts but is never immutable eligibility evidence. Deleting
or substituting an index item, payload descriptor, referenced materialization
file, CAS object, tool receipt, or evidence receipt invalidates every dependent claim; arbitrary SHA strings
have no authority.

The reservation file is deliberately transient rather than an acquisition-
index artifact. The final indexed evidence envelope embeds the exact immutable
reservation object, so its hash remains resolvable after the transient file is
unlinked. Verification recomputes it from the authorization, indexed intent,
and recorded nonce and rejects an envelope that lacks or changes that proof.

`authorizationId` is self-derived from the canonical authorization with its
ID/self-hash fields omitted; it is not a caller-chosen decision ID. Evidence
acquisition is a distinct `evidence:acquire` action under
`admission-evidence-acquire-v1`. It accepts one exact immutable HTTPS URL,
expected digest/bytes/media type, an explicit redirect set, and a one-use
authorization. It reuses the hardened manual-redirect/public-DNS/no-proxy/
no-credential/SSRF-resistant release downloader but can write only the derived
evidence-CAS path and cannot interpret archives or materialize source code.
Transfer stops at the authorization's hard byte cap. Task 4 performs no
network operation: its first zero census uses in-place materialization evidence
or truthful `local_unpublished_reference`. Only Task 7, after that census, may
invoke evidence acquisition for a measured, reviewed provenance deficit.

Evidence acquisition identity is strictly one-way: authorization -> prederived
payload descriptor, indexed invocation intent, and `wx` reservation -> CAS transaction (which binds
authorization/evidence/expected bytes, not a future receipt) -> completed
immutable primary-completion projection -> tool receipt -> acquisition receipt
-> final acquisition envelope.
The envelope is the durable
cross-object authority and binds every preceding ID/hash. No preceding object
names a later one. Construction-order tests reject the former
payload -> receipt -> transaction -> payload cycle.

The primary-completion object is no-clobber persisted and fsynced before either
nested child begins at the hash-derived contained path
`review/admission/evidence-cas/completions/$PRIMARY_COMPLETION_SHA256.json`.
Its self-hash covers exactly the stable transaction/input/network/final-byte
fields in `CalibrationEvidenceCasPrimaryCompletionV1`; the complete safe DNS/
redirect/peer/media observation is embedded, so deleting the transient
observation journal loses no authority. It
does not cover later mutable transaction state or handoff envelopes. The
acquisition receipt and envelope bind that projection hash. After the envelope,
payload/evidence generations, and acquisition-index generation are atomically
published, that same batch indexes the completion path/hash and envelope; the
indexed envelope is the CAS parent's durable completion marker.
Only then may recovery remove/fsync both completed nested handoffs, the CAS
transaction, reservation, and lock in their defined order. A crash anywhere in
that cleanup reopens the indexed envelope and primary completion rather than
rehashing a later journal state or refetching.

`evidence-bundle.json` is the fixed-path durable input to Task 1A's exported
factory. SlopBrick internally constructs its no-follow contained filesystem,
rehashes every real in-place/CAS byte, deep-freezes the validated object, and
registers that exact identity in a module-private `WeakSet`; the symbol alone
is not authority. A cast, clone, deserialization, fake filesystem, network
fallback, or object from another module instance fails. Task 1B and the final
context factory require membership in that WeakSet and exact evidence-context
hash equality, providing a checked one-way handoff rather than reconstructing
trust from plain data.

Invocation and receipt hashing is also acyclic. Before any mutation the tool
persists a `CalibrationAdmissionInvocationIntentV1`; CAS/census/source
transactions bind `invocationIntentId`, never a receipt that cannot yet exist.
After execution, `outputSetSha256` hashes the action schema's canonical
**primary-output projection**, with `toolReceiptSha256`, receipt IDs, envelope
self-hashes, and transaction self-hashes omitted exactly as enumerated by that
action schema. The post-execution tool receipt then binds that projection; the
final artifact envelope links the receipt and computes its own self-hash.
Implementations may not choose fields to omit dynamically. Tests mutate every
projected field and every omitted/link field, and cover a crash after the
pre-execution intent but before receipt creation.

`canonicalArgvSha256` is host-relocatable. Before hashing, every contained CLI
normalizes the actual corpus root, platform-commit root, prerequisite-staging
root, and transaction work root to the fixed logical tokens `@corpus`,
`@platform-commit`, `@prerequisite-staging`, and `@transaction-work`; contained
arguments are normalized relative paths. Absolute host roots may appear only in
an explicitly non-authoritative local diagnostic and never in an intent,
receipt, transaction output projection, or canonical artifact. Content identity
comes from the input-set hashes (including commit SHA and staging-set SHA), not
the host pathname. Fixtures relocate byte-identical roots and require identical
canonical argv, intent, receipt, and output hashes while rejecting an absolute
path embedded in any durable object.

Profiles, invocation intents, and tool receipts are immutable one-file-per-ID
objects under `tool-authority/`; the hash-linked, immutable-generation-backed
`tool-authority/index.json` is the only set authority. A single global `wx`
tool-authority lock/transaction serializes additions from census, register,
overlap, acquisition, and manifest actions, so unrelated actions cannot race a
shared JSONL replacement. The action intent is indexed before its first
mutation. Its owning output transaction remains recoverable until the later
receipt is indexed and reverified; only then may that output journal/lock be
removed. Tool-authority publication itself is the narrowly defined bootstrap
exception: it is governed by its schema-backed lock/transaction and does not
require another tool receipt, avoiding infinite regress. Verification replays
every index generation and rejects missing, duplicate, unindexed, or
substituted files. Cross-action concurrent-writer and crash-after-every-phase
tests prove no receipt/intent loss.

Bootstrap has one exact, acyclic order. The `create` transaction publishes
tool-authority generation 0 with the twelve frozen profile objects and empty
`invocationIntents`/`receipts` arrays. Only after that current index is durable
does a `replace` transaction index Task 0's invocation intent; Task 0 runs; a
later `replace` transaction indexes its receipt. Subsequent bootstrap actions
repeat intent-before-mutation and receipt-after-output. Generation 0 may contain
profiles only, and generation 1 or later may not add, remove, or mutate a frozen
profile. Validators reject a receipt in generation 0, an intent and its future
receipt in one pre-execution generation, a missing parent, or any `replace`
whose expected current hash is stale. Fault tests cover first-create recovery,
replacement recovery, and two writers racing an absent current index.

The infrastructure exception has one explicit operator:
`tool-authority:recover --root <root> (--transaction-id <id> | --from-lock)
--recovery-nonce <nonce> --acknowledge-no-live-writer`. It validates the lock,
stable transaction intent/current state hash, expected/current/next index,
immutable index generation, and every staged/final content-addressed object.
It rolls forward only a complete verified next generation; otherwise it
restores the prior index and removes only transaction-owned staging. It then
removes/fsyncs transaction before lock, never removes an unknown object, and is
idempotent after every write/promotion/fsync/unlink boundary. Because this is
the recursion-breaking tool-authority infrastructure operation, it intentionally
takes no ordinary tool profile/receipt.

Every parent transaction that invokes another publication uses the same
schema-backed nested-handoff rule; a jump from a parent phase to an already-
mutated child is invalid. The parent action schema enumerates its child slots
exactly. Before a child mutates anything, the parent freezes its complete child
input/expected-current contract and writes/fsyncs
`review/admission/nested-publications/$PARENT_TRANSACTION_ID/$CHILD_SLOT.json`
with `CalibrationNestedPublicationHandoffV1.state = started_fsynced`.
For `profiled_publication`, the parent first constructs the **complete**
canonical child invocation intent (profile, canonical argv, input set,
executable behavior, and network authorization), but it does not start the
profiled child. It derives the exact companion slot
`$CHILD_SLOT:intent-authority`, constructs the recursion-breaking tool-
authority lock/transaction that will add only that immutable intent, and
writes/fsyncs a `tool_authority_infrastructure` handoff for the companion slot.
The fixed tool-authority publisher then indexes the intent and completes that
handoff with the next immutable tool-index hash. Parent recovery always
recomputes/opens this companion first and uses the fixed tool-authority lock's
`intendedTransactionId`/recovery before it may create the output-child handoff.

Only after the companion completion and indexed intent revalidate does the
parent derive the profiled child's recovery nonce as the canonical SHA-256 of
`{parentTransactionId,parentRecoveryNonce,childSlot,childAction,childProfileId,
childInvocationIntentSha256,childInvocationIntentAuthorityIndexSha256,
expectedCurrentStateSha256}` plus domain string
`v10.3-child-recovery-nonce`. It then constructs the profiled child lock/
transaction and fsyncs the main handoff, which binds both the companion handoff
hash and intent-authority index, before the child mutates. For the recursion-breaking
`tool_authority_infrastructure` branch, there is intentionally no ordinary
profile, invocation intent, or receipt; the nonce instead hashes
`{parentTransactionId,parentRecoveryNonce,childSlot,
toolAuthorityObjectSetSha256,expectedCurrentStateSha256}` plus the same domain.
Only after the branch-specific nonce exists does the parent construct and
self-hash the complete child lock and immutable child transaction intent (all
frozen paths/limits). The handoff stores all required IDs/hashes and is fsynced
before the child mutates. A publisher-specific
proposal, when one exists, is referenced through the complete child's
`inputSetSha256`; publishers without proposals use their complete canonical
input set, so the generic handoff never invents a proposal object. The nonce
never hashes a lock/transaction that itself contains that nonce. Parent recovery recomputes the exact
companion/main handoff paths and nonces, revalidates the complete stored child
contracts, recovers intent authority first, then opens the one output-child
journal or proves it never started. A main profiled handoff without a completed
companion, or a child mutation before the intent-index generation, is invalid.
After child authority and receipt verify, the handoff becomes
`completed_fsynced` and adds the observed named primary-output projection and
next-authority hashes; neither is required or guessed in `started_fsynced`.
The generic handoff is transient coordination and remains until the parent
reaches its action-specific durable completion marker; it is then removed/
fsynced before the parent transaction/lock. Older acquisition, overlap, static,
and census completions do **not** claim post-cleanup handoff authority, because
their durable roots do not expose the parent transaction ID.

Only the new witness publication completion, prerequisite publication
completion, and manifest build receipt explicitly embed the complete
`completed_fsynced` handoff and bind the parent transaction. For those three
contracts, before the parent completion is frozen, the parent also no-clobber
writes/fsyncs the identical self-hashed immutable twin at
`nested-publication-completions/$PARENT_TRANSACTION_ID/$CHILD_SLOT.json`.
Any different-byte occupant is a hard collision; the twin is never replaced or
removed. Their post-cleanup verifiers derive that exact path from the embedded
parent/slot, compare the complete object byte-for-byte, and never list a
directory. Only after that comparison may the transient handoff be removed.

A completed infrastructure handoff uses
`childReceipt.kind = 'none_infrastructure'` and binds the next tool-authority
index as `childAuthoritySha256`; a profiled child must use the exact indexed
receipt branch. Supplying a fabricated ordinary receipt for infrastructure
publication, or omitting the receipt for a profiled child, is invalid.

The exact base child-slot sets and branches are:

- evidence CAS: infrastructure `evidence-tool-receipt`; profiled
  `evidence-metadata`;
- source round: infrastructure `source-intent-authority:$SOURCE_ID` for each
  sorted source before DNS, infrastructure
  `source-tool-receipt:$SOURCE_ID` for each source after its round-journal
  output, infrastructure `orchestrator-tool-receipt`, and profiled
  `source-metadata`;
- acquisition publication, register, and overlap: infrastructure
  `publication-tool-receipt`, `register-tool-receipt`, and
  `overlap-tool-receipt`, respectively;
- static rebuild: profiled `overlap-authority` and infrastructure
  `static-tool-receipt`;
- census: infrastructure `census-tool-receipt`;
- witness: infrastructure `search-publication-receipt` or
  `review-publication-receipt` as applicable (the search-computation receipt
  pre-exists the witness publication parent);
- manifest prerequisite publication and manifest generation: infrastructure
  `manifest-prerequisite-publication-tool-receipt` and
  `manifest-tool-receipt`, respectively.

For every base slot marked profiled, the exact required set also contains its
one `$BASE_SLOT:intent-authority` infrastructure companion; no infrastructure
base slot has that derived companion. The explicitly enumerated source-intent-
authority slots are separate preludes: each indexes the complete Git/release
child intent before the round transaction may perform DNS, while the source
network/temp/final output stays owned by
`CalibrationAcquisitionRoundTransactionV1`; the later source-tool-receipt slot
indexes its post-output receipt. A parent may not invent an extra slot, omit a base/
required companion, or reorder the sorted dynamic source slots. The CAS receipt/envelope bind the stable
`primaryCompletionSha256`, never the later coordination-journal self-hash.
Every owning task fault-tests the window immediately before and after companion
handoff fsync, tool-authority lock/transaction/current/fsync, companion
completion, main handoff fsync, output-child lock/transaction creation, child
current/index promotion, child receipt indexing, main handoff completion, and
parent completion/cleanup. Witness, prerequisite, and manifest publishers also
fault-test their immutable-twin write/fsync and embedded/twin equality. Recovery
never refetches, re-reviews, or removes an unknown path.

Evidence and pre-witness bundles bind a sorted
`CalibrationAdmissionToolAuthoritySnapshotV1` plus exactly the referenced
profile/intent/receipt objects, not the mutable current index. The snapshot
names an immutable historical index generation, so later unrelated receipts do
not stale an accepted bundle. A bundle never embeds its own producing receipt;
that later receipt resolves externally through its output projection and a
later tool-index generation. This keeps bundle creation acyclic while retaining
proof-carrying tool authority.

### 5.3 Verified admission context and authoritative audits

```ts
// Persisted plain data. Core owns its schemas/types/pure validators.
interface CalibrationAdmissionRecordStreamV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-record-stream-v1';

    readonly CalibrationRegisterGenerationReceiptV1[];

}

interface CalibrationAdmissionAuthorityCurrentV1 {

interface CalibrationAdmissionAuthorityRebuildLockV1 {
```
