```ts
interface AdmissionCohortInfeasibilityCertificateV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-infeasibility-v1';
  readonly gate: 'smoke' | 'canary';
  readonly eligibilitySnapshotSha256: string;
  readonly verifiedContextSha256: string;
  readonly algorithm: 'lexicographic-bnb-feasibility-v1';
  readonly proven: boolean;
  readonly proofKind:
    | 'capacity_cut'
    | 'exhaustive_search'
    | 'indeterminate_search_limit';
  readonly violatedConstraints: readonly string[];
  readonly certificateSha256: string;
}
```

Privacy results bind one exact admission record/content hash and contain only
fingerprints, never the matched secret or personal text. Any high-confidence
finding forces the corresponding status to `fail`. Low-confidence findings
force `review` until two blinded leakage/privacy decisions over the exact
finding set resolve them; a `pass` with findings, missing tool receipt,
missing/extra result, or reviewer decision over another record is invalid.
The privacy ledger's result/covered/unresolved sets must partition the complete
admission-record set exactly.

Every persisted interface above has a Core JSON Schema, generated type, pure
semantic validator, canonical self-hash rule, valid/invalid/semantic-invalid
fixtures, and mutation tests. Ledger IDs/edges/results are sorted; record sets
must match exactly with no missing/extra ID; Jaccard values are finite in
`[0,1]`; self-hashes omit only the self-hash field. A witness is the only
authority for `ready=true`. Marginal counts can set `countReady`, never
`ready`. The deterministic feasibility engine either emits an exact witness or
an infeasibility certificate. A search-limit certificate has `proven=false`
and blocks readiness; it is never reported as proof that no cohort exists.
`local_inventory_file` lets the overlap audit resolve already-present legacy
bytes through a local-only checkout map; it can complete overlap coverage but
can never satisfy an eligible materialization gate.
Universe validation enforces
`selectedAggregateCoverage = baselineMaterialUnits + repositoryMaterialUnits`,
`covered + unsupported + unreadable = selectedAggregateCoverage +
newCandidateUnits`, and exact equality between the JSONL candidate-ID set and
ledger coverage/unresolved sets. For the first census the first equation is
literally `452382 = 58089 + 394293`.
`newCandidateUnits` counts only candidate IDs outside that selected aggregate;
reviewing or promoting Monize or another legacy leaf reuses its existing IDs
and cannot inflate the universe.

The overlap authority consumes the canonical
`overlap-universe-records.jsonl` stream, not only the summary object. It
recomputes every row self-hash, polarity/side binding, ID set, and stream hash
before indexing. The summary's `recordsJsonlSha256` therefore cannot stand in
for missing rows. Every row binds `overlapSide`: an admission label derives
`ai_side`/`human_side`; otherwise the frozen intake declaration does; a
contradiction fails context construction. Edge rows repeat both endpoint
bindings/sides and exact integer intersection/union; `crossSide` is recomputed
rather than trusted, so legacy rows participate before they have admission
records. Edges, adjacency lists, connected-component summaries, and one-
member-per-row cluster memberships are separately sorted into <=64 MiB shards
and bound by shard receipts. The summary contains counts and ordered receipt
lists, never an unbounded `edges[]` or dense `memberCandidateUnitIds[]`.
Adjacency validation proves every edge appears at both endpoints; cluster
validation reconstructs components from the sharded adjacency stream,
reconciles bounded summary counts with sharded membership rows, and proves
every candidate appears in exactly one exact and one near cluster.

All authoritative shards and resumable checkpoints persist as generation-local
leaves under the exact hash-named
`review/admission/global/overlap/generations/$GENERATION_SHA256/`
subdirectories in Section 4; the work directory and flat projections are never
authority. `AdmissionBoundedShardReceiptV1.pathBase` is always literally
`generation_local`, so its normalized `relativePath` is resolved only inside
the generation pinned by `current-generation.json` (or an explicitly pinned
prior generation). Before inspecting current outputs, the
builder creates `publication.lock` with `wx`, binds the expected current
generation (or initial absence), and persists/fsyncs the stable transaction
intent. Two builders therefore cannot share an expected generation. Each
primary shard/checkpoint is written with `wx` under the transaction-owned
`staging-generation/` directory, hash/size/row-range checked, and fsynced. No
primary receipt contains a future final-generation path. The post-output static-ledger tool
receipt is then indexed through global tool authority; only afterward are the
receipt/ledger envelopes finalized. The complete artifact set is assembled with
`generation_local` leaf receipts in one staged generation directory; after its
generation hash is known, the whole directory is no-clobber promoted to
`global/overlap/generations/$GENERATION_SHA256` and the generations parent is
fsynced. Only then are optional current-output projections and
`current-generation.json` CAS-promoted, and all directories are fsynced.
Flat current-output projections, when emitted, are staged/promoted only after
the immutable directory and never participate in generation or shard
resolution. Checkpoint receipts bind the complete ordered input/output shard sets,
universe, normalizer, policy, invocation intent, and continuation cursor.
Verification reopens and rehashes every referenced shard. Missing, substituted,
overlapping-range, duplicate, out-of-order, or orphan shard/checkpoint files
fail artifact lint and context construction; interrupted unreferenced files are
removed only through their validated overlap-publication transaction.
`authority:overlap:recover (--transaction-id <id> | --from-lock)
--recovery-nonce <nonce>
--tool-profile admission-static-ledgers-v1 --acknowledge-no-live-writer`
validates the lock, expected/current generation CAS, stable intent/current
state hash, indexed tool receipt, immutable prior/next generations, and every
staged/final shard. It rolls forward a fully verified next generation or
restores every current output from the exact immutable prior generation; it
never removes an unknown path. Context construction refuses while either
journal exists. Recovery fsyncs outputs, removes/fsyncs transaction before
lock, and is idempotent after every write/promotion/tool-index/fsync/unlink
fault point, including first creation, replacement, and two concurrent writers.

Search artifacts also form an acyclic graph: the witness/certificate is
created first and contains no receipt ID; the later search receipt binds its
hash. The census binds both. A witness-review receipt is created only after the
witness exists, and the witness never references it.

---

## 6. Frozen eligibility predicate

### 6.1 Common immutable gates

All gold and sensitivity records require:

- a successfully constructed `VerifiedAdmissionContextV1`; no caller-supplied
  cast or record-embedded audit flag is accepted;
- registered HTTPS origin and immutable Git commit or checksum-pinned HTTPS
  release asset;
- every origin, rights, authorship, generator-revision, and reviewer claim
  resolves to an evidence-index item, schema-bound offline CAS payload, byte-
  matching verified receipt, and task-scoped tool receipt;
- one verified materialization receipt matching `materializationId`, source,
  repository, revision/asset, full archive materialization, and file bytes;
- closed inventory and source-review hash binding;
- exact locator, byte count, and SHA-256 match;
- static, complete scan-unit file with a supported language normalizer;
- approved analysis use;
- approved redistribution when the project creates/publishes a derived bundle;
- complete third-party rights chain, or `not_applicable` for wholly original
  generated output with an approved governing license;
- `familyId`, exact cluster, near cluster, and any applicable `pairGroupId`;
- a complete global overlap universe/authority and complete privacy/lineage
  and quality ledgers whose record and candidate-unit sets match exactly;
- zero high-confidence secret/PII/path disclosure in the selected file and in
  any distributed derived asset;
- no unresolved review result;
- two independent, agreeing reviewers plus a valid post-decision blind-review
  receipt whose assignment/evidence/decision sets match exactly;
- complete authority tool-profile/receipt coverage and a successful real-scale
  overlap resource receipt; a missing receipt or exceeded bound is not ready.

### 6.2 AI-positive gates

`eligible_gold` AI requires one of:

1. `generator_record` with provider/model identity, prompt/task binding,
   prompt/output hashes, generation timestamp, and `humanEditStatus = none`;
   a pinnable open model must carry its exact revision and generator source
   commit, while a hosted proprietary service may explicitly record
   `provider_not_exposed` and `hosted_service`; or
2. a benchmark attestation that binds the exact unit and independently records
   the same generator/edit facts in the bound evidence.

The immutable requirement applies to the evidence record and exact generated
output. `provider_not_exposed` is an evidence-backed reproducibility exception,
not a wildcard: its hosted product, provider/model alias, generation date,
immutable official provider-versioning evidence, two blinded accepting reviewer decisions,
prompt/output hashes, and no-edit status are mandatory and reverified. It is
forbidden when the evidence publishes a pinnable revision. Missing, local-only,
or stale exception evidence derives `generator_revision_missing`.

Repository attestation alone may produce `eligible_sensitivity` only when it
names the generator family, explicitly covers the exact file scope, and
resolves edit status as `none` or `light`. `light` is excluded from the strict
100/100 smoke and threshold fitting. `substantial` becomes `mixed_evaluation`;
`unknown` is quarantine.

A bare model alias without either a pinned revision or an explicit valid
`provider_not_exposed` record, broad “built with AI” wording, use of an AI tool
inside a project, and a repository's presence in the legacy positive arm do
not satisfy authorship.

### 6.3 Human-negative gates

`eligible_gold` human requires one of:

1. an official benchmark attestation that calls the set human/hand-written and
   binds the exact byte unit through a pinned revision; or
2. `historical_inference` where the exact blob was introduced and last changed
   by 2020-01-01, is reachable from the approved upstream history, is not a
   bulk import with unknown source, has an approved license, has no generator
   marker, and two reviewers explicitly accept the inference **and** the
   record binds a valid independent temporal attestation whose externally
   observed exact bytes predate the cutoff.

A complete Git graph without independent external pre-cutoff observation is
useful sensitivity evidence only; commit timestamps alone never authorize
human gold. Missing/invalid external evidence derives
`historical_attestation_missing`; shallow/grafted/replaced/incomplete history
derives `historical_graph_incomplete`.

An author/maintainer attestation may be added only through a new reviewed
evidence variant; it must not be squeezed into `historical_inference`.
Current repository popularity, a human-looking style, a negative folder, and
the absence of an AI disclosure are not human provenance.

### 6.4 Family, pair, cluster, overlap, and split gates

- `familyId` is the largest reviewed origin/dependency unit that could induce
  shared style or content: upstream repository/template for ordinary files;
  generator pipeline + source dataset for generated arms; never merely the
  current folder. A controlled human/AI transformation pair deliberately
  shares its origin family.
- A human/AI transformation pair uses one `pairGroupId`. Every member remains
  in one split, and an unsafe endpoint quarantines the entire pair group.
- Cross-polarity family membership is valid only when every cross-polarity
  connection is explained by a complete, approved transformation pair and the
  whole family remains in one split. Any unexplained cross-polarity membership
  is `unpaired_family_cross_polarity` and quarantines the family.
- Exact SHA-256 clustering runs globally across the legacy inventory and every
  new candidate. A cross-polarity exact cluster quarantines all endpoints.
- Near overlap uses versioned per-language normalization and 5-token shingles.
  Gold authority is a threshold-complete, disk-backed prefix-filter/inverted-
  index set-similarity join followed by exact Jaccard at inclusive `0.80`; its
  method ID is `prefix-filter-exact-jaccard-0.80-v1`. MinHash/LSH may run only
  as a separately labeled diagnostic accelerator because its current 0.80
  candidate probability is about 0.92 and cannot prove absence of an edge.
- A normalizer failure is `language_normalizer_unsupported`, never “no near
  overlap.”
- Every candidate pair, family, exact cluster, and near cluster is assigned to
  exactly one split before manifest construction. Cross-split membership is a
  hard failure.
- Same-polarity duplicates are represented once per content cluster in smoke
  and canary selection. Their additional provenance records remain in the
  census but do not increase unique eligible-unit counts.

The normalizer registry binds each language to a reviewed lexer/tokenizer
version, fixture corpus hash, strict UTF-8 policy, comment/string behavior, and
shingle policy. A language absent from the registry is unsupported. The exact
join externally sorts shingle postings into deterministic <=64 MiB shards,
orders tokens globally by frequency then shingle ID, uses the standard prefix
length `|x| - ceil(0.80 * |x|) + 1` plus safe length/position filters, spills
candidate pairs to sorted deduplicated runs, and computes exact set Jaccard for
every survivor. Common-shingle or pair expansion limits may stop with a
checkpoint receipt, but may never truncate silently: an exhausted disk/record/
pair budget sets `coverageComplete=false` and blocks readiness. Resume verifies
all shard, checkpoint, universe, registry, and tool hashes before continuing.

Unit/property fixtures are necessary but not scale acceptance. Before the
first census can become context-valid, the authority runs against the exact
452,382-row persisted universe stream and the real resolved source bytes, so
the receipt binds the observed language/token/shingle-frequency distribution,
not metadata-only dummy rows. The process runs under the frozen static-ledger
profile and records maximum RSS, work-directory bytes, open files, shard bytes,
and wall time in `AdmissionOverlapResourceReceiptV1`. Every configured limit is
actively enforced. A signal, resource exception, timeout, budget excess,
unreadable byte, or incomplete edge/cluster shard sets
`withinAllLimits=false` or `coverageComplete=false` and makes the context NOT
READY; it never converts the run into sampled or truncated authority.

The initial registry must account for the exact legacy language census:
TypeScript 228,456; Python 46,387; JavaScript 29,760; Go 28,520; Ruby 27,878;
C# 22,290; Java 19,404; C 16,009; Rust 10,489; Kotlin 9,747; C++ 4,231; SQL
2,839; PHP 2,061; Swift 1,886; Svelte 1,509; Dart 456; Astro 444; and `other`
16. Each named language gets its own registry entry (entries may share a
reviewed lexer implementation hash). Svelte/Astro template boundaries and
embedded languages require dedicated fixtures. The 16 `other` records must be
deterministically reclassified and normalized or remain explicitly unreadable;
they may not disappear. Until every row is covered, global gold readiness is
false.

All threshold arithmetic uses the exact rational `4/5`, never binary floating
point: candidate sizes satisfy `ceil(4|A|/5) <= |B| <= floor(5|A|/4)`, and the
required intersection is `ceil(4(|A|+|B|)/9)`. The final inclusive decision is
`5*intersection >= 4*union`. Prefix/length/position pruning must be proven
lossless by exhaustive small-set property tests; any optimization lacking that
proof is diagnostic-only.
Shingles use the full SHA-256 of length-delimited normalized token tuples, not
the current truncated 32-bit helper. A detected hash-to-different-tuple
collision is a hard authority failure, never an equal shingle.

The universe includes every one of the 452,382 selected legacy records plus
every new candidate, even when no admission record exists. It reports covered,
unsupported, and unreadable units. Any unresolved unit that could collide with
a proposed gold unit keeps `overlap_universe_incomplete` and
`overlap_authority_incomplete` active; exact hashes alone cannot clear unknown
near overlap.

### 6.5 Privacy, secrets, scaffold, and quality gates

- Scan every text member and printable strings from non-text members without
  importing or executing them.
- High-confidence private keys, credentials, access tokens, personal emails,
  phone/SSN patterns, or home-directory disclosures fail the affected record;
  a distributed archive containing them fails the whole asset.
- Low-confidence hits require blinded reviewer disposition; unresolved hits
  quarantine the record.
- A whole-file AI label fails when human prompt, canonical solution, license
  header, or benchmark scaffold accounts for more than 50% of normalized code
  bytes. A separately extracted target may be reconsidered only if its exact
  derivation is immutable and rights-approved.
- Syntax failure, truncated output, inert `pass`/placeholder target, or a code
  fragment that the scanner cannot treat as a complete file is diagnostic-only.

---

## 7. Exact census command and artifact

### 7.1 Commands

After vertical Tasks 1A-3B build and verify every prerequisite, run exactly:

```bash
corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick build

SMOKE_SEARCH_JSON="$(corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- \
  witness:search \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --gate smoke \
  --tool-profile admission-census-v1)"
SMOKE_SEARCH_BUNDLE_RELATIVE_PATH="$(node -e \
  'const x=JSON.parse(process.argv[1]);process.stdout.write(x.relativePath)' \
  "$SMOKE_SEARCH_JSON")"
SMOKE_SEARCH_BUNDLE_SHA256="$(node -e \
  'const x=JSON.parse(process.argv[1]);process.stdout.write(x.sha256)' \
  "$SMOKE_SEARCH_JSON")"
SMOKE_SEARCH_COMPLETION_RELATIVE_PATH="$(node -e \
  'const x=JSON.parse(process.argv[1]);process.stdout.write(x.completionRelativePath)' \
  "$SMOKE_SEARCH_JSON")"
SMOKE_SEARCH_COMPLETION_SHA256="$(node -e \
  'const x=JSON.parse(process.argv[1]);process.stdout.write(x.completionSha256)' \
  "$SMOKE_SEARCH_JSON")"

CANARY_SEARCH_JSON="$(corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- \
  witness:search \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --gate canary \
  --tool-profile admission-census-v1)"
CANARY_SEARCH_BUNDLE_RELATIVE_PATH="$(node -e \
  'const x=JSON.parse(process.argv[1]);process.stdout.write(x.relativePath)' \
  "$CANARY_SEARCH_JSON")"
CANARY_SEARCH_BUNDLE_SHA256="$(node -e \
  'const x=JSON.parse(process.argv[1]);process.stdout.write(x.sha256)' \
  "$CANARY_SEARCH_JSON")"
CANARY_SEARCH_COMPLETION_RELATIVE_PATH="$(node -e \
  'const x=JSON.parse(process.argv[1]);process.stdout.write(x.completionRelativePath)' \
  "$CANARY_SEARCH_JSON")"
CANARY_SEARCH_COMPLETION_SHA256="$(node -e \
  'const x=JSON.parse(process.argv[1]);process.stdout.write(x.completionSha256)' \
  "$CANARY_SEARCH_JSON")"

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- census \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --smoke-search-bundle "$SMOKE_SEARCH_BUNDLE_RELATIVE_PATH" \
  --smoke-search-bundle-sha256 "$SMOKE_SEARCH_BUNDLE_SHA256" \
  --smoke-search-publication-completion "$SMOKE_SEARCH_COMPLETION_RELATIVE_PATH" \
  --smoke-search-publication-completion-sha256 "$SMOKE_SEARCH_COMPLETION_SHA256" \
  --canary-search-bundle "$CANARY_SEARCH_BUNDLE_RELATIVE_PATH" \
  --canary-search-bundle-sha256 "$CANARY_SEARCH_BUNDLE_SHA256" \
  --canary-search-publication-completion "$CANARY_SEARCH_COMPLETION_RELATIVE_PATH" \
  --canary-search-publication-completion-sha256 "$CANARY_SEARCH_COMPLETION_SHA256" \
  --tool-profile admission-census-v1 \
  --out review/eligible-census-v10.3.json

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- verify \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --tool-profile admission-census-v1 \
  --census review/eligible-census-v10.3.json

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- require \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --tool-profile admission-census-v1 \
  --census review/eligible-census-v10.3.json \
  --gate smoke
```

Each `witness:search` invocation prints one canonical JSON object containing
only its hash-derived bundle `relativePath`/`sha256` and publication
`completionRelativePath`/`completionSha256`; capture those exact values above.
`census` rejects a path not derived from the gate/kind/hash, rehashes the
complete bundle and completion/tool receipt, and performs no directory
discovery. When a reviewed witness bundle exists, add the analogous exact
`--smoke-witness-review-bundle{,-sha256}` plus
`--smoke-witness-review-publication-completion{,-sha256}` pairs (or the four
canary equivalents).

Exit contract:

- `census`: exit 0 when it truthfully writes a valid census, even when counts
  are zero; exit 2 on malformed/tampered inputs or an existing output file
  unless an exact reviewed compare-and-swap hash is supplied.
- `verify`: exit 0 only when canonical regeneration is byte-identical and all
  input hashes still match; exit 2 otherwise.
- `require --gate smoke|canary`: exit 0 when that gate is ready, exit 1 when
  evidence is valid but insufficient, and exit 2 when evidence is invalid.

The first run against normalized current evidence must report valid evidence
with both eligible-gold unique-unit cells equal to zero, `smoke.countReady =
false`, `smoke.ready = false`, a bound infeasibility certificate, and exit 0.
The subsequent `require --gate smoke` must exit 1. A zero census must never be
described as “clean,” “passed,” or “ready.”

After source evidence changes, do not delete or casually overwrite the zero
census. Re-run `census` with
`--replace-if-current-sha $EXPECTED_CURRENT_FILE_SHA256`. The CLI must verify
that exact current file hash under an exclusive sibling lock.

```ts
interface CalibrationCensusLockV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-census-lock-v1';
  readonly lockId: string;
  readonly intendedTransactionId: string;
  readonly operation: 'create' | 'replace';
  readonly expectedCurrentJsonSha256?: string;
  readonly expectedCurrentSidecarSha256?: string;
  readonly nextJsonSha256: string;
  readonly nextSidecarSha256: string;
  readonly nextJsonTemporaryRelativePath: string;
  readonly nextSidecarTemporaryRelativePath: string;
  readonly historyJsonRelativePath?: string;
  readonly historySidecarRelativePath?: string;
  readonly recoveryNonce: string;
  readonly invocationIntentId: string;
  readonly lockSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationCensusTransactionV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-census-transaction-v1';
  readonly transactionId: string;
  readonly lockSha256: string;
  readonly invocationIntentId: string;
  readonly operation: 'create' | 'replace';
  readonly expectedCurrentState:
    | { readonly kind: 'absent_pair' }
    | {
        readonly kind: 'existing_pair';
        readonly jsonSha256: string;
        readonly sidecarSha256: string;
      };
  readonly nextJsonSha256: string;
  readonly nextSidecarSha256: string;
  readonly nextJsonTemporaryRelativePath: string;
  readonly nextSidecarTemporaryRelativePath: string;
  readonly historyJsonRelativePath?: string;
  readonly historySidecarRelativePath?: string;
  readonly state:
    | {
      readonly phase:
          | 'intent_fsynced'
          | 'history_json_fsynced'
          | 'history_sidecar_fsynced'
          | 'history_directory_fsynced'
          | 'next_json_temporary_fsynced'
          | 'next_sidecar_temporary_fsynced'
          | 'temporary_directory_fsynced'
          | 'json_promoted'
          | 'sidecar_promoted'
          | 'pair_verified'
          | 'output_directory_fsynced'
          | 'temporaries_removed'
          | 'temporary_removal_fsynced';
      }
    | {
        readonly phase:
          | 'tool_receipt_indexed'
          | 'commit_complete';
        readonly toolReceiptId: string;
        readonly toolReceiptSha256: string;
        readonly toolAuthorityIndexSha256: string;
        readonly toolAuthorityPublicationTransactionId: string;
      };
  readonly transactionSha256: string;
}
```

Persist/fsync the pre-execution invocation intent, then create
`eligible-census-v10.3.lock` with `wx` **before** inspecting output state;
write its complete recovery envelope, fsync the lock and parent directory, then
write/fsync the transaction intent. `create` requires both current outputs
absent; `replace` requires both present, valid, and exactly equal to the
supplied CAS hashes. One-present/one-absent is always recovery-required, never
treated as create. Two writers therefore cannot both pass CAS.

For replace, copy both current files no-clobber into hash-named history and
fsync each file and directory. For both operations, write/fsync two uniquely
named, transaction-bound sibling temporaries, fsync their directory, promote
JSON then sidecar, verify the resulting pair, and fsync the output directory.
Then remove only hash-matching transaction temporaries, fsync that removal,
derive the census action's post-execution tool receipt from the verified output
projection and publish it through the single global tool-authority
lock/transaction/index. Only after that indexed receipt revalidates may the
census transaction persist/fsync `commit_complete`, remove/fsync
the transaction **while the lock still excludes new writers**, and finally
remove/fsync the lock. Phases
through `commit_complete` are persisted before their mutation boundary. An
unlink cannot record a phase inside the unlinked artifact: transaction and lock
removal completion is inferred from artifact presence plus the lock envelope
and final pair. The lock repeats operation, expected/next hashes, temp/history
paths, and recovery nonce, so it can safely finish the narrow interval after
transaction removal. The lock is derived first from the immutable invocation
intent and operation envelope and stores the already-derived
`intendedTransactionId`; the later transaction binds `lockSha256` and repeats
that intent ID. Transaction identity excludes the lock hash, so this remains
one-way rather than a hash fixed point. The census does not embed
its own producing receipt; artifact lint resolves the output projection to the
canonical tool log. A crash after output promotion but before receipt
publication therefore remains recoverable under the still-present lock/journal.

`census:recover (--transaction-id <id> | --from-lock)
--recovery-nonce <nonce>
--acknowledge-no-live-writer` validates the transaction's one-way lock hash,
their matching invocation-intent IDs,
current pair, both temporaries, history, and phase before mutation. For create,
it rolls forward only when both verified next bytes exist; otherwise it removes
only a partial output whose hash equals the recorded next hash and restores the
required absent pair. For replace it rolls forward when verified next bytes
exist, otherwise restores the exact verified history pair. It also completes
interrupted temporary removal, lock removal/fsync, transaction removal/fsync,
including crashes after either artifact was unlinked but before its directory
fsync. Transaction cleanup always precedes lock cleanup; recovery never removes
the lock while an old transaction still exists, so a new writer cannot race an
old transaction unlink. There is no time-based automatic stale-lock break. Unknown/mismatched
files are never removed. Wrong IDs/nonces, ambiguous live-writer state,
same-path/different-byte history or temporary, one-sided unknown output, or an
unrecognized phase exit 2 without mutation. Tests kill the writer before and
after lock-file fsync, lock-directory fsync, transaction-intent fsync, and every
later file mutation **and** fsync for first-create and replacement. The lock-
only recovery test uses `--from-lock` and no transaction ID, recomputes the
intended ID, and safely restores/continues without knowledge of an unwritten
transaction. Tests also start
two simultaneous writers, exercise occupied history/temp/output collisions,
and prove roll-forward, rollback-to-absence, history restore, transaction-then-
lock cleanup, and repeated recovery are idempotent.

### 7.2 Artifact shape

```ts
interface CensusSourceRow {
  readonly sourceId: string;
  readonly sourceKind: 'aggregate_inventory' | 'material_source';
  readonly contributesToAdditiveCounts: boolean;
  readonly sourceInventoryClosed: boolean;
  readonly sourceInventoryCandidateUnits: number;
  readonly admissionRecords: number;
  readonly unrepresentedCandidateUnits: number;
  readonly uniqueContentUnits: number;
  readonly dispositions: CensusDispositionMatrix;
  readonly sourceDecision: 'candidate' | 'source_quarantine';
  readonly sourceReasons: readonly AdmissionReason[];
}

interface CensusLanguageRow {
  readonly language: string;
  readonly eligibleGoldVerifiedAiUniqueUnits: number;
  readonly eligibleGoldVerifiedHumanUniqueUnits: number;
  readonly aiFamilyCount: number;
  readonly humanFamilyCount: number;
}

interface CensusFamilyRow {
  readonly familyId: string;
  readonly materialSourceIds: readonly string[];
  readonly polaritySet: readonly AdmissionLabel[];
  readonly pairGroupIds: readonly string[];
  readonly pairedCrossPolarity:
    | 'not_cross_polarity'
    | 'approved_paired'
    | 'unpaired_conflict';
  readonly countsByLabel: Readonly<Record<AdmissionLabel, CensusCountPair>>;
  readonly dispositions: CensusDispositionMatrix;
}

interface CensusCountPair {
  readonly records: number;
  readonly uniqueUnits: number;
}

type CensusDispositionMatrix = Readonly<Record<
  AdmissionDisposition,
  {
    readonly total: CensusCountPair;
    readonly byLabel: Readonly<Record<AdmissionLabel, CensusCountPair>>;
  }
>>;

interface CalibrationAdmissionCensusV103 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-census-v1';
  readonly policyVersion: 'v10.3-admission-v1';
  readonly policySha256: string;
  readonly smokeWitnessPolicySha256: string;
  readonly canaryWitnessPolicySha256: string;
  readonly eligibilitySnapshotSha256: string;
  readonly sourceRegisterSha256: string;
  readonly verifiedContextSha256: string;
  readonly evidenceIndexSha256: string;
  readonly evidencePayloadSetSha256: string;
  readonly evidenceReceiptSetSha256: string;
  readonly toolProfileSetSha256: string;
  readonly toolReceiptSetSha256: string;
  readonly blindReviewReceiptSetSha256: string;
  readonly temporalAttestationSetSha256: string;
  readonly materializationReceiptSetSha256: string;
  readonly admissionRecordsSha256: string;
  readonly sourceReviewSetSha256: string;
  readonly overlapUniverseSha256: string;
  readonly overlapResourceReceiptSha256: string;
  readonly overlapLedgerSha256: string;
  readonly privacyLedgerSha256: string;
  readonly qualityLedgerSha256: string;
  readonly lineageLedgerSha256: string;
  readonly counts: {
    readonly openSourceCount: number;
    readonly sourceInventoryCandidateUnits: number;
    readonly admissionRecords: number;
    readonly unrepresentedCandidateUnits: number;
    readonly uniqueContentUnits: number;
    readonly dispositions: CensusDispositionMatrix;
    readonly bySource: readonly CensusSourceRow[];
    readonly byLanguage: readonly CensusLanguageRow[];
    readonly byFamily: readonly CensusFamilyRow[];
    readonly recordRejectionReasons: Readonly<Record<AdmissionReason, number>>;
    readonly sourceBlockerReasons: Readonly<Record<AdmissionReason, number>>;
  };
  readonly smoke: {
    readonly targetVerifiedAi: 100;
    readonly targetVerifiedHuman: 100;
    readonly deficitVerifiedAi: number;
    readonly deficitVerifiedHuman: number;
    readonly countReady: boolean;
    readonly witnessSha256?: string;
    readonly searchResultBundleSha256: string;
    readonly searchResultBundleRelativePath: string;
    readonly searchResultPublicationCompletionSha256: string;
    readonly searchResultPublicationCompletionRelativePath: string;
    readonly witnessReviewBundleSha256?: string;
    readonly witnessReviewBundleRelativePath?: string;
    readonly witnessReviewPublicationCompletionSha256?: string;
    readonly witnessReviewPublicationCompletionRelativePath?: string;
    readonly infeasibilityCertificateSha256?: string;
    readonly ready: boolean;
    readonly gateFailures: readonly string[];
  };
  readonly canary: {
    readonly targetVerifiedAi: 5000;
    readonly targetVerifiedHuman: 5000;
    readonly deficitVerifiedAi: number;
    readonly deficitVerifiedHuman: number;
    readonly minimumSourceCheckoutsPerPolarity: 10;
    readonly availableSourceCapacityVerifiedAi: number;
    readonly availableSourceCapacityVerifiedHuman: number;
    readonly sourceCapacityDeficitVerifiedAi: number;
    readonly sourceCapacityDeficitVerifiedHuman: number;
    readonly countReady: boolean;
    readonly witnessSha256?: string;
    readonly searchResultBundleSha256: string;
    readonly searchResultBundleRelativePath: string;
    readonly searchResultPublicationCompletionSha256: string;
    readonly searchResultPublicationCompletionRelativePath: string;
    readonly witnessReviewBundleSha256?: string;
    readonly witnessReviewBundleRelativePath?: string;
    readonly witnessReviewPublicationCompletionSha256?: string;
    readonly witnessReviewPublicationCompletionRelativePath?: string;
    readonly infeasibilityCertificateSha256?: string;
    readonly ready: boolean;
    readonly gateFailures: readonly string[];
  };
}

interface CalibrationAdmissionEvidenceBundleV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-evidence-bundle-v1';
  readonly policy: CalibrationAdmissionPolicyV1;
  readonly witnessPolicies: readonly [AdmissionWitnessPolicyV1, AdmissionWitnessPolicyV1];
  readonly toolProfiles: readonly CalibrationAdmissionToolProfileV1[];
  readonly invocationIntents: readonly CalibrationAdmissionInvocationIntentV1[];
  readonly toolReceipts: readonly CalibrationAdmissionToolReceiptV1[];
  readonly toolAuthoritySnapshot: CalibrationAdmissionToolAuthoritySnapshotV1;
  readonly evidenceIndex: CalibrationAdmissionEvidenceIndexV1;
  readonly evidencePayloadSet: CalibrationAdmissionEvidencePayloadSetV1;
  readonly approvedEvidenceAcquisitions:
    readonly CalibrationApprovedEvidenceAcquisitionV1[];
  readonly evidenceAcquisitionReceipts:
    readonly CalibrationEvidenceAcquisitionReceiptV1[];
  readonly evidenceAcquisitionEnvelopes:
    readonly CalibrationEvidenceAcquisitionEnvelopeV1[];
  readonly acquisitionAuthoritySnapshot: CalibrationAdmissionAcquisitionSnapshotV1;
  readonly evidenceReceipts: readonly CalibrationAdmissionEvidenceReceiptV1[];
  readonly materializationReceipts:
    readonly CalibrationAdmissionMaterializationReceiptV1[];
  readonly bundleSha256: string;
}

declare const verifiedAdmissionEvidenceContextBrand: unique symbol;
type VerifiedAdmissionEvidenceContextV1 = Readonly<{
  readonly evidenceContextSha256: string;
  readonly bundle: CalibrationAdmissionEvidenceBundleV1;
  readonly [verifiedAdmissionEvidenceContextBrand]: true;
}>;

declare function buildVerifiedAdmissionEvidenceContext(
  root: string,
  input: unknown,
): Promise<
  | { readonly ok: true; readonly context: VerifiedAdmissionEvidenceContextV1 }
  | { readonly ok: false; readonly errors: readonly string[] }
>;
```

Both deficit pairs are computed from
`counts.dispositions.eligible_gold.byLabel.*.uniqueUnits`; record counts are
reported for audit but never reduce a deficit twice for duplicate bytes.
For each source,
`sourceInventoryCandidateUnits = admissionRecords + unrepresentedCandidateUnits`.
`recordRejectionReasons` counts affected admission records;
`sourceBlockerReasons` counts affected sources. A source-wide blocker is never
multiplied by a raw file estimate and presented as a record-level result.
Every register entry has exactly one source row, including unreviewed or
source-wide-quarantined entries, so an omitted source fails verification.
An open source inventory may report only its exactly inventoried lower bound;
`sourceInventoryClosed = false`, `openSourceCount`, and
`source_inventory_open` prevent that number from being mistaken for a complete
denominator or an eligible source.
Aggregate rows reconcile child coverage but are excluded from additive global
counts. Every admission record appears in exactly one disposition/label cell;
each cell's `uniqueUnits <= records`; all material-source record totals equal
the global admission-record total; and no material candidate belongs to two
material sources. The four disposition matrices are complete even when zero.
Reason counts are multi-valued diagnostics and are **not** required to sum to
rejected records. Source blockers count sources only.

`countReady` means marginal quantities are sufficient to attempt deterministic
feasibility. `ready` is true only when `witnessSha256` resolves to a schema-
valid, context-bound witness and independent regeneration/reverification
passes, its acyclic search receipt matches, and an approved schema-valid
witness-review bundle embeds the exact search-result bundle and binds two blinded
decisions, blind receipt, review receipt, and two independent byte-identical
regenerations. A missing witness-review bundle, a proven infeasibility certificate, or an
indeterminate search-limit certificate keeps `ready=false` even when all
marginals pass.
`eligibilitySnapshotSha256` hashes the canonical input hashes, disposition
matrix, and joint eligible-unit rows before witness/status fields. Witnesses
bind that non-circular snapshot plus `verifiedContextSha256`; the final census
then binds the witness or certificate hash.
The artifact has no current time, duration, hostname, username, or absolute
path. Arrays sort by stable IDs; reason maps contain every vocabulary key,
including zeros. `eligible-census-v10.3.sha256` contains exactly
`$LOWERCASE_SHA256  eligible-census-v10.3.json\n`, where the variable is the
digest of the adjacent canonical JSON file.

Object identity hashes use the existing `canonicalSha256` convention: UTF-8
canonical JSON with recursively sorted object keys and no trailing LF. A
serialized `.json` artifact is `canonicalJson(value) + "\n"`, and its sidecar
checksum hashes those exact file bytes. `sourceRegisterSha256` hashes the
complete register object; `sourceReviewSetSha256` hashes the canonical array of
source-review hashes sorted by `sourceId`; `admissionRecordsSha256` hashes the
exact canonical JSONL bytes sorted by `recordId` and terminated by one LF when
non-empty. Decision JSONL inputs sort by canonical target and then
`reviewerId`. Duplicate IDs, unsorted accepted input, or a missing registered
source are hard errors rather than normalizations performed silently.

### 7.3 What the census does not do

- It does not crawl directories to discover eligibility.
- It does not generate a corpus manifest or selection.
- It does not materialize a source or access the network.
- It does not trust a source-specific `eligibleFiles` summary without
  reconstructing every eligible record.
- It does not count multiple same-content records as multiple unique units.
- It does not use ad hoc balancing or random sampling. It invokes the frozen
  exact cohort-feasibility authority and binds its witness/certificate.
- It does not silently drop a registered source or confuse an unnormalized
  candidate unit with an eligible, rejected, or nonexistent record.

---

## 8. Smoke and canary thresholds

The numeric diversity floors below operationalize the existing project docs'
“multiple repositories/languages” and “several independent families” language.
They are conservative project policy, not a claim that internet literature
proves these exact cutoffs. Changing them after seeing outcomes requires a new
policy/method version and independent review.

`lexicographic-bnb-feasibility-v1` orders canonical counting owners by the
Section 3 selection key, branches include-before-exclude, uses only integer
constraints, and returns the lexicographically smallest feasible sorted key
vector. Frozen search ceilings are 10,000,000 nodes for smoke and 50,000,000
for canary. Exhaustion emits a deterministic `proven=false` certificate and
blocks readiness; it does not authorize a heuristic cohort. Constraint,
candidate-order, branch-count, pruning-count, and terminal hashes are bound in
the search receipt.

### 8.1 Strict mechanics smoke

The smoke selection is exactly 100 unique-content `eligible_gold` AI records
and exactly 100 unique-content `eligible_gold` human records; each selected
record is the canonical counting owner of a different content cluster. It is a
pipeline/mechanics test, not a general performance or multi-language claim.
The exact 200 IDs come only from a verified `AdmissionCohortWitnessV1`; passing
source/language/family marginals alone is insufficient.

Admission readiness requires:

- all 200 satisfy the gold evidence routes in Sections 6.2-6.3, not
  sensitivity-only repository attestations;
- all AI records have `humanEditStatus = none`;
- no exact/near/unpaired-family cross-polarity conflict and no unsafe pair
  group;
- at least 100 unique content clusters per polarity;
- all privacy, rights, syntax, and materialization gates pass;
- at least two languages, with at least 20 unique units from each polarity in
  each represented smoke language;
- at least two independent source checkouts and at least three independent
  families per polarity;
- no source checkout or family contributes more than 50 units to one polarity.

A 100/100 cohort that misses one of those diversity gates may be run only as
an explicitly exploratory diagnostic. It leaves `smoke.ready = false`, cannot
close corpus admission, and cannot feed threshold or release decisions.

Execution acceptance, after the separate manifest/run work is authorized:

- 200/200 selected records resolve and hash-match before scanning;
- at least 196/200 scans succeed overall;
- at least 95/100 succeed in each polarity and at least 95% succeed in every
  language/polarity stratum;
- absolute polarity success-rate gap is at most 2 percentage points within
  each represented language;
- any repository has at most 10% failed scans;
- zero-fire, timeout, terminal failure, retry/bisection, and resume behavior is
  forced through controlled fixtures alongside the real cohort;
- two independent runs produce byte-identical normalized observations,
  coverage, and rule counts after removing only explicitly non-semantic runtime
  durations;
- all failures are enumerated, and a passing smoke changes no rule threshold.

### 8.2 Exact 10k canary

The canary selection is exactly 10,000 unique-content gold units: 5,000 AI and
5,000 human canonical counting owners.
It may begin only after the 100/100 smoke passes and a new census says
`canary.ready = true`.

Admission readiness requires:

- at least five independent families per polarity;
- at least ten source checkouts per polarity, derived exactly from
  `ceil(5000 / 500) = 10`; census reports available per-polarity source
  capacity and deficit;
- at least three AI generator/model families;
- at least three represented languages;
- each represented language has at least 250 unique gold units per polarity
  and at least three families per polarity;
- no family exceeds 20% (1,000) of one polarity;
- no repository/source checkout exceeds 10% (500) of one polarity, unless an
  independent reviewer documents an unavoidable benchmark grouping and the
  selection is downgraded to diagnostic;
- no same-content cluster contributes more than one selected unit;
- all paired/derived units remain group-disjoint across train/validation/test;
- no unresolved license, privacy, edit, model revision, or materialization
  gate;
- selection is deterministic from a preregistered seed and policy.

Several separately authorized rounds may therefore be required after smoke;
the two-source acquisition-round cap is not represented as sufficient to make
canary feasible. `canary.ready` requires the exact 10,000-unit witness, not the
ten-source marginal alone.

Execution acceptance keeps the existing v10.3 coverage gates:

- 100% resolve/hash verification before scan;
- at least 98% successful scans overall;
- at least 95% successful in every language/polarity stratum;
- no repository has more than 10% failed scans;
- polarity completion gap per language is at most 2 percentage points;
- two-run normalized metrics and accounting are byte-identical;
- a failed gate makes the canary diagnostic-only and blocks method freeze.

A standalone language claim remains stricter: at least 1,000 gold units and
five independent families **in each polarity** for that language.

### 8.3 Full-calibration population

This source-admission plan does not invent a fixed full-run count before the
canary. After canary coverage/power review and method freeze, “use all” means
all records that remain `eligible_gold` under the frozen manifest inclusion,
balance, family, pair, cluster, and split policy. It never means every raw file,
container row, directory member, sensitivity record, or quarantined record in
`corpus-expansion`. The reviewed post-canary census freezes the exact full-run
number.

---

## 9. Conditional public-source acquisition policy

No network acquisition occurs before a reviewed census. Afterward, compute:

```text
aiDeficit    = max(0, targetAi -
  dispositions.eligible_gold.byLabel.verified_ai.uniqueUnits)
humanDeficit = max(0, targetHuman -
  dispositions.eligible_gold.byLabel.verified_human.uniqueUnits)
reviewTarget = max(16, ceil(max(aiDeficit, humanDeficit) * 1.25))
```

Also carry the exact unresolved diversity failures from `smoke.gateFailures`
(language floors, source count/cap, and family count/cap) as
`diversityDeficits`; do not turn them into invented file-count arithmetic.
First prefer remediation of already-present, high-provenance sources. A new
public pull is allowed only if a count deficit is non-zero **or** at least one
diversity deficit remains, the owner authorizes the acquisition round, and a
metadata-only preflight passes. When only diversity is missing,
`reviewTarget = 16` is the bounded initial review, not a promise that 16 files
will close the gate.

After smoke, canary planning separately reports, per polarity, distinct
eligible source checkouts, capped capacity `sum(min(eligibleUnitsAtSource,
500))`, the 5,000-unit capacity deficit, and the derived minimum of ten
checkouts. Each further maximum-two-source round needs a new reviewed census
and authorization; no round is presumed sufficient.

### 9.1 Preflight requirements

Before cloning/downloading bytes, record:

- official HTTPS origin;
- full immutable commit or release-asset URL + byte count + SHA-256;
- explicit license URL/hash and scope for source code, dataset, and generated
  output as applicable;
- item-level or exact-set authorship evidence;
- generator/model/edit fields for AI candidates or accepted human evidence;
- a stable family/pair key;
- declared size and file/record format;
- whether source code is already present elsewhere in the canonical workspace.

Reject the pull before bytes when any of those are absent. A tag or branch is a
locator, never immutable identity.

### 9.2 Bounded acquisition round

- Acquire at most two new sources per round.
- Cap materialized bytes at 5 GiB total per round. For release assets, also
  enforce a 5 GiB streamed HTTP transfer cap. Stock Git cannot guarantee a
  network-transfer-byte ceiling: its materialized/blob/pack bytes are measured,
  but network transfer is explicitly `not_hard_bounded`. If the owner's round
  authorization requires a hard transfer ceiling, Git acquisition is forbidden
  and the decision remains `not_acquired`.
- Do not initialize submodules or Git LFS automatically. Each needs a separate
  size/hash/license approval.
- Store each source exactly once under `sources/benchmarks/$SOURCE_ID` using a
  temporary sibling and atomic rename after hash/revision checks.
- Do not create positive/negative copies.
- Add/update the source register and closed inventory in the same evidence
  batch.
- Do not create a manifest, selection, or run in an acquisition round.

Raw shell is not an acquisition authority. The approved decision and canonical
receipt use Core schemas:

```ts
interface CalibrationAcquisitionRoundAuthorizationV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-acquisition-round-authorization-v1';
  readonly roundId: string;
  readonly approvedBy: string;
  readonly approvedAt: string;
  readonly parentCensusSha256: string;
  readonly measuredDeficitsSha256: string;
  readonly sourceAuthorizationIds: readonly [string] | readonly [string, string];
  readonly maxSources: 2;
  readonly maxTotalMaterializedBytes: number; // <= 5 GiB
  readonly authorizationSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationApprovedAcquisitionV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-approved-acquisition-v1';
  readonly authorizationId: string;
  readonly approvedBy: string;
  readonly approvedAt: string;
  readonly sourceId: string;       // safe slug, not a path
  readonly repositoryId: string;
  readonly materializationId: string;
  readonly originUrl: string;      // credential-free HTTPS only
  readonly transport:
    | {
        readonly kind: 'git_https';
        readonly commitSha: string; // exactly 40 lowercase hex
        readonly transportByteLimit: 'not_enforceable_by_stock_git';
        readonly ownerAcknowledgedUnboundedTransport: true;
      }
    | {
        readonly kind: 'release_https';
        readonly materialization: ReleaseArchiveMaterialization;
        readonly maxTransferBytes: number; // <= 5 GiB
        readonly approvedRedirectUrls: readonly string[];
      };
  readonly maxMaterializedBytes: number; // <= 5 GiB safe integer
  readonly licenseEvidenceId: string;
  readonly licensePath: string;    // safe normalized relative path
  readonly licenseSha256: string;  // 64 lowercase hex
  readonly authorizationSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationAcquisitionReceiptV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-acquisition-receipt-v1';
  readonly receiptId: string;
  readonly authorizationId: string;
  readonly roundId: string;
  readonly authorizationSha256: string;
  readonly sourceId: string;
  readonly repositoryId: string;
  readonly materializationId: string;
  readonly originUrl: string;
  readonly transport:
    | {
        readonly kind: 'git_https';
        readonly commitSha: string;
        readonly treeSha: string;
        readonly observedPackBytes: number;
        readonly observedNetworkBytes: 'not_observable_exactly';
      }
    | {
        readonly kind: 'release_https';
        readonly materialization: ReleaseArchiveMaterialization;
        readonly extractionReceipt: MaterializationReceiptV1;
        readonly observedTransferBytes: number;
        readonly redirectChain: readonly string[];
      };
  readonly materializedBytes: number;
  readonly inventorySha256: string;
  readonly licenseSha256: string;
  readonly materializationReceiptId: string;
  readonly materializationReceiptSha256: string;
  readonly networkObservation: {
    readonly requestUrl: string;
    readonly redirectChain: readonly string[];
    readonly resolvedPublicAddresses: readonly string[];
    readonly connectedPeerAddress: string;
  };
  readonly resolvedPublicAddressesSha256: string;
  readonly connectedPeerEvidenceSha256: string;
  readonly transactionId: string;
  readonly toolReceiptId: string;
  readonly toolReceiptSha256: string;
  readonly receiptSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationAcquisitionRoundReceiptV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-acquisition-round-receipt-v1';
  readonly receiptId: string;
  readonly roundId: string;
  readonly parentCensusSha256: string;
  readonly sourceReceiptSha256s: readonly [string] | readonly [string, string];
  readonly sourceInvocationIntentIds: readonly [string] | readonly [string, string];
  /** Canonical round-authorization order; profile hashes may repeat. */
  readonly sourceProfileSha256s: readonly [string] | readonly [string, string];
  readonly sourceToolReceiptSha256s: readonly [string] | readonly [string, string];
  readonly orchestratorInvocationIntentId: string;
  readonly orchestratorToolReceiptId: string;
  readonly orchestratorToolReceiptSha256: string;
  readonly toolAuthoritySnapshot: CalibrationAdmissionToolAuthoritySnapshotV1;
  readonly acquiredSourceCount: 1 | 2;
  readonly totalMaterializedBytes: number;
  readonly withinAuthorizedCountAndBytes: true;
  readonly receiptSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationAcquisitionRoundLockV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-acquisition-round-lock-v1';
  readonly lockId: string;
  readonly intendedTransactionId: string;
  readonly roundId: string;
  readonly orchestratorInvocationIntentId: string;
  readonly sourceInvocations: readonly {
    readonly authorizationId: string;
    readonly invocationIntentId: string;
    readonly profileId: 'admission-git-acquire-v1' | 'admission-release-acquire-v1';
    readonly profileSha256: string;
  }[];

  readonly maxTotalMaterializedBytes: number;
  readonly recoveryNonce: string;
  readonly lockSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationAcquisitionRoundTransactionV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-acquisition-round-transaction-v1';
  readonly transactionId: string;
  readonly lockSha256: string;
  readonly roundId: string;
  readonly orchestratorInvocationIntentId: string;
  readonly sourceInvocations: readonly {
    readonly authorizationId: string;
    readonly invocationIntentId: string;
    readonly profileId: 'admission-git-acquire-v1' | 'admission-release-acquire-v1';
    readonly profileSha256: string;
  }[];
  readonly maxTotalMaterializedBytes: number;
  readonly reservedMaterializedBytes: number;
  readonly recoveryNonce: string;
  readonly sources: readonly {
    readonly authorizationId: string;
    readonly temporaryRelativePath: string;
    readonly finalRelativePath: string;
    readonly expectedIdentitySha256: string;
    readonly maxMaterializedBytes: number;
    readonly networkObservationRelativePath: string;
    readonly sourceReceiptTemporaryRelativePath: string;
    readonly sourceReceiptFinalRelativePath: string;
    readonly materializationReceiptTemporaryRelativePath: string;
    readonly materializationReceiptFinalRelativePath: string;
    readonly toolReceiptTemporaryRelativePath: string;
    readonly state:
      | { readonly phase: 'not_started' | 'transport_complete' }
      | {
          readonly phase:
            | 'network_observation_fsynced'
            | 'tree_verified'
            | 'temporary_fsynced'
            | 'destination_promoted'
            | 'destination_directory_fsynced';
          readonly networkObservationSha256: string;
        }
      | {
          readonly phase: 'materialization_receipt_staged_fsynced';
          readonly networkObservationSha256: string;
          readonly childToolReceiptId: string;
          readonly childToolReceiptSha256: string;
          readonly toolAuthorityIndexSha256: string;
          readonly materializationReceiptId: string;
          readonly materializationReceiptSha256: string;
        }
      | {
          readonly phase: 'source_receipt_staged_fsynced';
          readonly networkObservationSha256: string;
          readonly childToolReceiptId: string;
          readonly childToolReceiptSha256: string;
          readonly toolAuthorityIndexSha256: string;
          readonly materializationReceiptId: string;
          readonly materializationReceiptSha256: string;
          readonly sourceReceiptId: string;
          readonly sourceReceiptSha256: string;
        };
  }[];
  readonly state:
    | { readonly phase: 'intent_fsynced' | 'all_sources_verified' | 'all_destinations_promoted' }
    | {
        readonly phase: 'orchestrator_tool_receipt_indexed';
        readonly orchestratorToolReceiptId: string;
        readonly orchestratorToolReceiptSha256: string;
        readonly toolAuthorityIndexSha256: string;
      }
    | {
        readonly phase: 'round_receipt_staged_fsynced';
        readonly orchestratorToolReceiptId: string;
        readonly orchestratorToolReceiptSha256: string;
        readonly toolAuthorityIndexSha256: string;
        readonly roundReceiptId: string;
        readonly roundReceiptSha256: string;
        readonly roundReceiptTemporaryRelativePath: string;
      }
    | {
        readonly phase: 'metadata_publication_complete' | 'complete';
        readonly orchestratorToolReceiptId: string;
        readonly orchestratorToolReceiptSha256: string;
        readonly toolAuthorityIndexSha256: string;
        readonly roundReceiptId: string;
        readonly roundReceiptSha256: string;
        readonly roundReceiptTemporaryRelativePath: string;
        readonly acquisitionIndexSha256: string;
        readonly acquisitionPublicationTransactionId: string;
        readonly materializationReceiptLedgerSha256: string;
        readonly evidenceBundleSha256: string;
      };
  readonly transactionSha256: string;
}

interface CalibrationAdmissionAcquisitionIndexV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-admission-acquisition-index-v1';
  readonly generation: number;

      | 'evidence_authorization'

      | 'round_receipt'

    | { readonly kind: 'absent' }

interface CalibrationAcquisitionPublicationLockV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-acquisition-publication-lock-v1';

  readonly invocationIntentId: string;

    | { readonly kind: 'absent' }
    | { readonly kind: 'existing'; readonly indexSha256: string };

  readonly artifactSetSha256: string;
  readonly recoveryNonce: string;

interface CalibrationAcquisitionPublicationTransactionV1 {
  readonly version: 'v10.3-acquisition-publication-transaction-v1';
  readonly transactionId: string;
  readonly lockSha256: string;
  readonly invocationIntentId: string;
  readonly operation: 'create' | 'replace';
  readonly expectedCurrentState:
    | { readonly kind: 'absent' }
    | { readonly kind: 'existing'; readonly indexSha256: string };
  readonly nextIndexSha256: string;
  readonly artifacts: readonly {
    readonly stagedRelativePath: string;
    readonly finalRelativePath: string;
    readonly bytes: number;
    readonly sha256: string;
  }[];
  readonly immutableIndexGenerationRelativePath: string;
  readonly nextIndexTemporaryRelativePath: string;
  readonly state:
    | {
        readonly phase:
          | 'intent_fsynced'
          | 'artifacts_staged_fsynced'
          | 'artifacts_promoted'
          | 'index_generation_fsynced'
          | 'next_index_temporary_fsynced'
          | 'index_promoted'
          | 'output_directories_fsynced';
      }
    | {
        readonly phase: 'publication_tool_receipt_indexed' | 'complete';
        readonly publicationToolReceiptId: string;
        readonly publicationToolReceiptSha256: string;
        readonly toolAuthorityIndexSha256: string;
      };
  readonly transactionSha256: string;
}
```

Schemas reject unknown keys, unsafe slug/path characters, path containment
escapes, non-HTTPS/credentialed origins, mutable revisions, bad digests,
non-safe integers, excess size, unresolvable authorization/evidence IDs, and a
destination already present.

Acquisition metadata authority is the schema-valid `acquisitions/index.json`,
not directory discovery. Every update first publishes a no-clobber hash-named
index generation under `acquisitions/index-generations/`, then CAS-replaces the
current index under the publication lock/transaction. Verification replays the
complete parent-hash chain from generation 0 and rehashes every indexed
authorization/receipt/envelope path. Missing history, an unindexed artifact,
or an indexed missing/substituted artifact fails context construction. The
`acquisition:authorize` local action publishes reviewed proposal artifacts;
network actions publish their source/evidence/round receipts and evidence
envelope as one later indexed batch. An evidence batch also stages/fsyncs the
next evidence index, payload set, verification-receipt ledger, and durable
evidence bundle, writes immutable copies under `evidence-generations/`, and
promotes all current files before the acquisition index last. The publication
index binds every one of those hashes; a new envelope with a stale payload set,
receipt ledger, or evidence bundle is invalid. Both use a separate publication intent
and `admission-acquisition-publication-v1` receipt. A crash leaves the transaction
and lock recoverable through acquisition-index promotion, indexing of that
post-output publication receipt in global tool authority, and cleanup; neither
is removed earlier. The prior index remains authoritative before promotion;
no raw append or singular
receipt output is canonical.

Evidence/pre-witness bundles bind a sorted snapshot of an already-immutable
**parent** acquisition-index generation, never the current index object that
will later index the bundle. Publication order is parent index -> bundle -> next
index generation. The next index binds the bundle hash; no bundle hashes an
index that hashes that same bundle. Construction-order fixtures include
generation 0 and reject the former bundle/index fixed point. Concretely, the
first `acquisition:publish --operation create` writes an empty generation-0
index (`artifacts = []`, no parent). The generation-0 evidence bundle snapshots
that immutable empty index. A later `--operation replace` writes generation 1,
whose artifact set indexes the evidence index, payload set, receipt ledger, and
bundle. A bundle may snapshot only a strict ancestor index; semantic validation
rejects a same-generation or descendant snapshot and any generation-0 index
that already names its bundle.

A completed source round's indexed batch also contains one verified
`CalibrationAdmissionMaterializationReceiptV1` per source, the next immutable
materialization-receipt ledger generation/current ledger, and the rebuilt
evidence bundle that references them. Register deltas may refer only to those
indexed receipt IDs/hashes. Publishing source/round receipts without the
materialization objects/ledger/evidence-bundle generation is invalid and leaves
the register unchanged.

The ledger authority is the canonical JSONL at
`review/admission/materialization-generations/$LEDGER_SHA256.jsonl`, indexed as
`materialization_receipt_ledger` by the same acquisition generation. It is one
canonical receipt object per line, sorted/unique by `receiptId`; filename hash,
stream hash, count, receipt ID set, and every receipt hash are recomputed. The
fixed `materialization-receipts.jsonl` is only a same-batch byte-identical
projection. Its exact ID/hash set must equal the evidence bundle's sorted
`materializationReceipts` set; missing, extra, duplicated, reordered,
substituted, unindexed, or projection-only receipt bytes invalidate context.

The source authorization carries the exact `repositoryId`, derived
`materializationId`, and lossless Git commit or complete
`ReleaseArchiveMaterialization` (`assetUrl`, bytes, digest, `archiveFormat`,
`rootPrefix`, and `extractionPolicy`). After the stable acquisition transaction
ID, primary materialized-output/tree hash, and child tool receipt exist, the
materialization receipt proves immutable repository/materialization identity
plus the verified unit set. It references no final mutable transaction self-hash
and deliberately contains no source-review or future source-receipt hash. The
later source acquisition receipt binds that materialization receipt and the
round receipt binds the source receipt. Because byte proof contains no review
hash, a later review promotion cannot stale it. After those receipts
and evidence-bundle generation are indexed, reviewers audit the acquired
inventory, rights, authorship, and labels; only the resulting blinded decisions
may freeze a source generation. That source generation references the stable
materialization receipt, and the later register delta binds both. The strict
one-way order is authorization -> transaction/child tool receipt ->
materialization receipt -> source receipt -> round receipt -> acquisition index
and evidence bundle -> blinded review/source generation -> register delta.

`acquisition:recover-publication` is the generic recovery entry for every
acquisition-index update, including authorization-only updates with no CAS or
round transaction. It validates expected/current/next index generations,
staged/final artifacts, publication tool receipt in global tool authority, and
the recovery nonce; it rolls forward a complete batch or restores the exact
prior index, removes no unknown file, then unlinks/fsyncs publication
transaction before lock. Repeated recovery and crashes at every boundary are
idempotent.

Round, authorization, and receipt IDs are canonical self-derived IDs, never
operator-supplied labels. Both Git and release receipts use the transport-
neutral `toolReceiptId` plus `toolReceiptSha256`; semantic validation requires
that receipt's exact transport profile/action and keeps the ID distinct from
its digest. One `acquire:round` command serializes the entire
one- or two-source round under `acquisition-round.lock`; standalone per-source
network acquisition is not exposed. Before DNS it persists the round intent,
lock, and transaction and reserves the **sum** of both per-source maxima. The
lock/transaction/round receipt bind the offline
`admission-acquisition-round-v1` orchestrator intent plus the
`{authorizationId, invocationIntentId, profileId, profileSha256}` tuple for
each Git/release child capability in the explicit canonical order of the
round authorization's `sourceAuthorizationIds`; the round receipt also
records child profile hashes and tool-receipt hashes (profile hashes may
repeat). Cross-profile substitution is invalid. The sum must fit the one 5 GiB
ceiling. It downloads/materializes each source into its
transaction-bound temporary, verifies all sources, and only then no-clobber
promotes them. A failure before all promotions rolls back only exact
transaction-owned paths. Each source's DNS/redirect/peer observations and
source/tool receipts are staged/fsynced in transaction-owned paths before its
one-use authorization can be considered consumed. `acquire:recover` requires
the round ID, recovery nonce, and no-live-writer acknowledgement; it validates
the exact lock/transaction/source journals, completes or rolls back the whole
round, stages each source/materialization receipt, delegates the atomic
materialization-ledger/evidence-bundle/index promotion to the exact
acquisition-publication transaction recorded by the round journal, then
removes/fsyncs the metadata-publication transaction, round transaction, and
locks in that order. It never refetches, re-reviews, or deletes unknown paths and is
idempotent after every transport/promotion/receipt/index/unlink/fsync crash.
The durable source receipt embeds the complete safe request/redirect/resolved-
address/connected-peer observation and hashes its address/peer projections;
the round journal's observation file is transient. Receipt validation
recomputes those hashes, so journal cleanup cannot leave an unaddressable
observation, and deletion/substitution tests mutate every embedded field.
Each child tool receipt and the post-output round-orchestrator receipt are
indexed in the global tool authority before acquisition metadata publication;
the final round receipt binds all of them plus the immutable tool snapshot and proves both
the count and cumulative-byte ceiling, so two independent 5 GiB sources cannot
be authorized or run concurrently.

The only authorization/acquisition operator interfaces are:

```bash
corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- acquisition:publish \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --publication-proposal review/admission/acquisitions/proposals/$PROPOSAL_ID.json \
  --operation create \
  --expect-current-absent \
  --tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- acquisition:publish \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --publication-proposal review/admission/acquisitions/proposals/$PROPOSAL_ID.json \
  --operation replace \
  --expected-current-index-sha256 $CURRENT_INDEX_SHA256 \
  --tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- acquisition:authorize \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --proposal review/admission/acquisitions/proposals/$PROPOSAL_ID.json \
  --tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- acquisition:recover-publication \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --from-lock \
  --recovery-nonce $PUBLICATION_RECOVERY_NONCE \
  --tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1 \
  --acknowledge-no-live-writer

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- acquire:round \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --round-authorization review/admission/acquisitions/authorizations/round/$ROUND_ID.json \
  --source-authorization review/admission/acquisitions/authorizations/source/$SOURCE_AUTHORIZATION_ID_1.json \
  --source-authorization review/admission/acquisitions/authorizations/source/$SOURCE_AUTHORIZATION_ID_2.json \
  --round-tool-profile admission-acquisition-round-v1 \
  --publication-tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1 \
  --git-tool-profile admission-git-acquire-v1 \
  --release-tool-profile admission-release-acquire-v1 \
  --authorization-sha256 $APPROVED_ROUND_AUTHORIZATION_SHA256 \
  --network allow

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- evidence:acquire \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --authorization review/admission/acquisitions/authorizations/evidence/$EVIDENCE_AUTHORIZATION_ID.json \
  --tool-profile admission-evidence-acquire-v1 \
  --publication-tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1 \
  --authorization-sha256 $APPROVED_EVIDENCE_AUTHORIZATION_SHA256 \
  --network allow

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- evidence:recover \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --transaction-id $TRANSACTION_ID \
  --recovery-nonce $RECOVERY_NONCE \
  --tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1 \
  --acknowledge-no-live-writer

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- acquire:recover \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --from-lock \
  --recovery-nonce $RECOVERY_NONCE \
  --round-tool-profile admission-acquisition-round-v1 \
  --publication-tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1 \
  --acknowledge-no-live-writer

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- register:publish-round \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --proposal review/admission/register-generations/proposals/$DELTA_ID.json \
  --expected-current-register-sha256 $CURRENT_REGISTER_SHA256 \
  --tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1

corepack pnpm --filter slopbrick run cal:admission -- register:recover \
  --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3 \
  --from-lock \
  --recovery-nonce $REGISTER_RECOVERY_NONCE \
  --tool-profile admission-acquisition-publication-v1 \
  --acknowledge-no-live-writer
```

`--source-authorization` is repeatable exactly one or two times. The CLI
canonicalizes by authorization ID, rejects duplicates, and requires exact
equality with the round authorization's ordered ID set; the second line above
is omitted for a one-source round.

Each `git_https` source must use exactly `admission-git-acquire-v1`; each
`release_https` source must use exactly `admission-release-acquire-v1`; an
unused profile is not invoked and any cross-mapping exits 2 before DNS. Each transport receipt binds the complete resolved
public-address set and connected-peer observation (or the reviewed Git/cURL
behavior proof that cryptographically pins that set) rather than merely
repeating the requested hostname.

`--network` defaults to `deny`; omission cannot fetch. The exact one-use
authorization hash, selected network profile, source/transport, and canonical
decision must all match before any DNS or socket operation. Census/context/
ledger processes have no network capability object. The CLI derives the
contained destination itself and uses a cryptographically random, `wx`, no-
clobber sibling temporary directory.

Neither acquisition command may be invoked before Task 4 has persisted,
verified, and independently reviewed the initial zero census. Implementing or
behavior-probing the denied/default path is not an acquisition. After that
boundary, evidence acquisition may fetch only a preflighted proof object;
source acquisition additionally requires the measured census deficit and
owner-authorized round in Section 9.

Git runs by absolute reviewed executable ID with an argument array (no shell)
and a minimal allowlisted environment: fresh contained `HOME` and
`XDG_CONFIG_HOME`, `GIT_CONFIG_NOSYSTEM=1`, `GIT_CONFIG_GLOBAL=/dev/null`,
`GIT_TERMINAL_PROMPT=0`, disabled askpass/credential helpers/hooks/filters,
`protocol.allow=never`, `protocol.https.allow=always`, and only the exact
approved HTTPS origin. SSH, `git://`, file, ext/remote-helper, submodule, LFS,
proxy, alternate object directory, replace-ref, graft, and inherited Git config
surfaces are rejected. Before Git starts, the network authority resolves every
A/AAAA address, rejects private, loopback, link-local, multicast, reserved, or
mixed public/private sets, and binds the approved public set into the Git/cURL
invocation using behavior-probed `http.curloptResolve`; redirects are disabled
with `http.followRedirects=false`. The receipt binds the DNS answer set and,
where the probed Git/cURL exposes it, the connected peer. If this Git build
cannot prove address pinning and redirect denial, Git network acquisition is
unsupported rather than allowed with a weaker check. It fetches the exact commit into an isolated bare object
store, enumerates the tree with `ls-tree -rz`, rejects symlinks, submodules,
special types, unsafe/colliding paths, and LFS pointers, and materializes regular
blobs with `cat-file` plus `wx`; it never invokes checkout filters or candidate
code.

Release acquisition delegates to the shared release-asset downloader. It uses
manual redirects, accepts only the preapproved credential-free HTTPS URL set,
clears proxy/netrc/credential environment, rejects userinfo, downgrade, private
or loopback destinations and DNS-rebinding address changes, streams through
the hard byte counter, verifies the asset digest before safe extraction, and
exposes no generic fetch client to source adapters. Git and release network
capabilities are distinct and cannot be substituted.
Streamed byte counters enforce the materialized cap. It verifies license,
closed inventory, commit/tree, file hashes, containment, and receipt before
atomic promotion. Any network, validation, or receipt failure removes only its
unique temporary directory and leaves the destination absent.

Tests use injected Git and HTTPS transports plus denied-by-default DNS/socket/
spawn sentinels. They prove exact-origin capability use, all other network
attempts fail, argument non-injection, isolated config/hooks/filters/
credentials/proxies, malicious trees, Git private/mixed DNS, Git rebinding and
redirect attempts, release redirects/DNS rebinding, LFS/
submodule rejection, honest Git unbounded-transport acknowledgement, HTTP
stream/materialized limits, destination containment, no-clobber, interruption
cleanup, and canonical receipt verification.
Exact commands for HTTP release assets come from the release-asset
materialization plan and must retain its no-network-by-default scan boundary.

### 9.3 Pull stop conditions

Stop acquiring immediately when any condition holds:

- the smoke census reaches `ready = true`, including 100/100 and all diversity
  gates; end the smoke acquisition campaign and do not pull “extra” before
  Task 10. Acquisition may resume for Task 11 only from a fresh reviewed
  canary census/deficit, with a new owner-authorized round and the canary stop
  conditions below;
- the canary census reaches `ready=true` with its exact 5,000/5,000 witness,
  ten-source-per-polarity minimum, and all diversity caps;
- a source-wide license, rights, or authorship gate fails;
- two consecutive review batches admit fewer than 10% of reviewed logical
  units;
- source inventory differs from its upstream declaration by more than 1% or
  by any unexplained identity mismatch;
- high-confidence secrets/PII occur in more than 0.1% of sampled units or in a
  distributed source artifact;
- an adapter would need to execute candidate code;
- the transfer/review budget is exceeded;
- the owner has not authorized publication, maintainer contact, gated access,
  or another acquisition round.

When stopped, update the census and rejection counts. Do not compensate by
relaxing a frozen gate.

---

## 10. Reviewer roles and independence

| Role | Responsibility | May not do |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Intake operator | Pin/acquire source, close inventory, record hashes | Approve their own source |
| Authorship reviewer A | Blindly assess AI/human evidence scope and edit status | See reviewer B's decision first |
| Authorship/rights reviewer B | Independently assess label plus license/use scope | Reuse A's rationale as their decision |
| Leakage/privacy reviewer | Reproduce exact/near/family/pair and secret/PII audits | Change the label policy to rescue a source |
| Adjudicator | Resolve A/B disagreements; quarantine when unresolved | Count a disagreement as agreement |
| Tooling reviewer | Review schemas, verifier, census determinism, mutation tests | Approve evidence they generated |
| Calibration reviewer | Approve census-to-manifest transition and smoke/canary gates | Treat admission as calibration success |

Structured decision IDs—not bare reviewer tuples—are required on every
candidate/eligibility-bearing source review and every reviewed record. The
explicit generation-0 `source_quarantine + review_incomplete + []` leaf is the
only no-decision source-review state and authorizes nothing. Semantic validation proves distinct identities,
pre-decision blind assignment, a matching post-decision blindness receipt,
role coverage, exact reviewed evidence IDs, rights approval, and any
adjudication links. Decisions never contain peer IDs or the later receipt ID;
the receipt contains both sealed decision IDs. The adapter implementer and intake
operator may not be the sole final reviewers. Disagreement remains
`review_disagreement` until a distinct adjudicator links both decisions;
silence is `review_incomplete`.

---

Corepack pnpm, package engine/API/build target) blocks Task 1A. Probe failures
are otherwise profile-scoped: read-only Git behavior blocks only slices that
need Git bytes; the Git-network profile blocks Task 7 Git acquisition only;
Python/pyarrow blocks only the Droid portion of Task 6; release-network probes
block release acquisition only; `jq`, `du`, and `shasum` are diagnostic and
never gate authority. The bootstrap commit does not claim a canonical receipt.
Task 1A defines profile/receipt contracts and reruns each probe; thereafter a
missing/red canonical receipt blocks only actions owned by that exact profile.
